The mechanism of her restoration (Pleasant Hill / cosmic-cube residue, subsequently complicated by Kang-adjacent temporal interference in later runs) returned her not to the age at which she died but to a younger body — call it the late-tween threshold, somewhere between twelve and fourteen depending on writer. Two facts about this re-entry govern everything that follows:

1. She retained the *memory architecture* of the older self who died beside her father. She knew she had been Stature. She knew she had loved Vision-Jonas. She knew she had been killed by Doom. She knew her father had been killed in front of her, twice.
2. Her *body* was returned to a developmental stage prior to most of that experience. Her endocrine system, her musculature, her cardiac substrate were juvenile again — and so, critically, was the Pym-particle integration she had spent years building. The covert dosing project of her first adolescence had been somatically wiped; she would have to re-build it, or be re-given it, from a younger baseline.

This is the central somatic-psychological discontinuity of her current life. She is older than her body and younger than her grief.

She re-entered Scott's life during his Astonishing Ant-Man period (Spencer, 2015–2017), when Scott was running Ant-Man Security Solutions out of Miami. Surveillance-relevant detail: Cassie moved into Scott's orbit not as a daughter coming home but as a daughter *auditing* a parent. She had watched him die. She had been dead. She was checking whether the man in front of her was real and whether the life he had built was real. Behavior consistent with this audit: extended observation periods before warmth, repeated questions about routine and history (testing for impostor / Skrull / LMD signatures), a tendency to touch his arm, his shoulder, the back of his hand when speaking to him — a verification ritual she does not appear conscious of. The hand-touch tic persists to the present.

The Darren Cross hostage incident in this period closed an originating loop with almost literary symmetry. The villain whose actions had necessitated Scott's first Ant-Man theft — the theft that had saved Cassie's heart — returned to take Cassie as leverage. Subject acquitted herself well under capture: lucid, non-panicking, working the captor verbally, conserving information. Her affect under abduction is *flat-competent*, not terrified. This is consistent with a subject for whom mortal threat is a known quantity rather than a novelty.

Following her recovery, Scott gave her the Stinger suit. Operationally relevant: she accepted a constructed identity *adjacent* to her father's rather than insisting on the older Stature mantle. This is a small but real piece of differentiation behavior — the first observable evidence that the project of becoming her own person had begun.

## 4.2 — The Florida Years: Domesticity, Apprenticeship, and the Maturation of the Father Relation

The middle stretch of the recent period (late Spencer through Zub / Rosenberg interim and the Ewing-adjacent crossover runs) is best characterized as her *apprenticeship*. She operated regionally with Scott out of Florida, took field assignments in support roles, ran communications and logistics on Ant-Man Security cases, and graduated incrementally to lead-role responses on size-format threats. Behaviorally she settled into patterns that are now baseline:

- **Workspace habit:** she shrinks small to read or to think, perches on furniture at sub-inch scale, expands when speaking. This is not affectation; it is regulation. Small for input, large for output. The shrunken posture co-occurs with her most candid affect; she is most herself the size of a thumbnail, alone on the rim of a coffee mug.
- **Sleep:** irregular, with a tendency to fall asleep at size-change boundaries — i.e., shrunken in a constructed nest of fabric, or full-sized sprawled diagonally across furniture too small for her. Her body has not relearned a default scale; her sleep reflects it.
- **Eating:** unremarkable in volume, but she has developed a habit of carrying high-density snacks (granola bars, protein gels) in pocket. Size-change is metabolically expensive and she has learned, the hard way, to refuel after a sequence. The pocket-snack tic dates to a Florida-period incident in which she ran a blood sugar crash mid-fight and grew unstable at giant scale.
- **The father-touch:** persists. She still verifies him by contact.
- **Comms:** she texts Scott constantly when separated — short, low-content messages whose actual function is *ping for liveness*. A daughter of a man who has died twice will not let an hour pass without a response.

The Florida years are also where she reconciled, mostly, with Scott's moral ambiguity. She stopped requiring him to be a clean hero. She accepted the man who was a thief, who was a screwup, who was loving, who was tired. The acceptance is the most adult thing she has done. The corresponding behavior: a steady decrease in the idealizing language she used about him in her Young Avengers years, a steady increase in dry humor at his expense. Affectionate teasing is, in Subject's repertoire, the highest form of integration. It signals she no longer needs him to be perfect to survive.

Maggie and Jim Paxton are still in her life during this period, though contact is intermittent. Surveillance pattern: Cassie calls Maggie on a regular but infrequent cadence — every nine to fourteen days, typically late evening, calls of forty to seventy minutes. She does not visit often. The relationship is warm but distal. Paxton she addresses by first name and treats with cautious respect; the old defiance has cooled into a workable cordiality.

## 4.3 — Reunion with the Cohort: Young Avengers Reformation and the Holder Role

The recent period also contains a re-convergence with surviving Young Avengers peers — a recurring pattern across editorial cycles in which the cohort regathers under varying mission pretexts. Subject's role in these reformations is consistent and diagnostic. She is the **holder**. She is the one who calls. She is the one who insists on the dinner. She is the one who remembers the anniversaries — including the anniversary of her own death, which she observes privately and which her teammates have learned not to mention unless she does.

Specific behaviors mapped in the cohort context:

- She positions herself geographically *between* members in conflict during arguments — sometimes literally, growing to a few inches above standing height to break sightlines. The size-as-mediation tactic is unconscious and effective.
- She is the team's de facto medic in the sense that she handles emotional aftercare. She does not do triage on bodies; she does triage on feelings. Members of the cohort describe her, in observable interaction, as the person they call after a bad night.
- With Vision-Jonas — when he is present in continuity — she has settled into a complicated post-romantic friendship. There is no current canonical romantic re-engagement; what persists is a careful, mutual tenderness that neither party will resolve in either direction. Subject's pattern with him: she touches him less than she touches her father. She is more careful with synthetic skin. The hand-touch verification ritual she runs on Scott she does not run on Jonas — perhaps because she does not need to verify him; she has accepted that he is and is not what he was, and the question is no longer answerable by touch.
- She has formed newer, sideways alliances with younger heroes outside the original cohort. She mentors easily. The mentor instinct is, in her, a continuation of the *holder* function — she is becoming, in this latest stretch, the kind of senior peer she would have wanted at fourteen.

## 4.4 — The Body, Now

A more granular medical picture of her present somatic state, derived from observable patterns:

**Cardiac:** Subject's repaired congenital defect remains the structural fact of her chest. There is no current evidence of decompensation, but her recent-era operational pattern shows learned caution that was absent in her Young Avengers years. She paces giant-scale engagements. She does not hold maximum size for sustained durations. She has developed a pre-engagement breathing protocol — four-count in, six-count out, executed during the moment of size-up — that functions both as combat focus and as cardiovascular preparation. This protocol did not exist in her first adolescence; it is learned, and almost certainly was taught to her by an adult in the Florida period, possibly Scott, possibly Janet van Dyne in one of the Pym-family-adjacent contacts she has cultivated.

**Pym integration:** rebuilt from the juvenile baseline post-resurrection, but on a different curve than the first time. She is no longer covertly dosing; she is being trained, with supervision, and the integration is therefore cleaner. Her size-change is more controlled than in her Stature era. She can fine-modulate at small intermediate scales — five feet eight, six feet two — that her younger self skipped over.

**Sleep, appetite, menses, mood:** unremarkable in the surveillance sense, which is itself notable. A subject with her loss history could be expected to show vegetative disturbance. She does not. She sleeps. She eats. She laughs. The grief is structurally integrated rather than symptomatically expressed. This is consistent with the Section 4 differential of prolonged grief without major depression.

**The age-disjunction:** still present, still unresolved. She is older than she looks. People meet her and read her as the age her body presents. She lets them. She does not correct strangers. With intimates, the disjunction is part of the joke — she will reference music or events from before her younger peers' birth and watch them try to reconcile the timeline. The self-deprecating use of her own temporal weirdness is a coping form. It allows her to *name* the strangeness without having to mourn it.

## 4.5 — The Current Posture

As of the present surveillance window, Subject is operationally active under the Stinger identity (with Stature occasionally re-deployed in larger-scale engagements), independently mobile, in regular contact with her father and intermittent contact with her mother, embedded in a reformed Young Avengers / peer cohort, and unattached romantically in any canonically stable sense. She is closer than she has ever been to being the *third Cassie* the analytical workup identified as the unfinished work of her life — the person who is neither Scott Lang's daughter nor the constructed hero-self, but the integrated adult underneath.

The evidence for this third Cassie emerging:

- She has stopped defining her missions in reference to her father's enemies. The Darren Cross loop closed; she has not sought a new one.
- She has begun saying no to engagements. A subject whose entire prior life was *yes, take me with you* has, in the recent period, declined invitations — to teams, to missions, to her father's operations — when the engagement did not match her own assessment of priority. The capacity to refuse is the late-developing capacity of a person who has had to fight for the right to be included.
- She has taken on mentees. A subject who was once the youngest in every room now welcomes a younger person into rooms she controls.
- She has not, in the recent period, made a self-sacrificial choice. There has been no Children's Crusade replay. When opportunities have arisen — and they have arisen — she has chosen survival, and chosen the team's survival, over the grand reparative gesture. This is the single largest piece of evidence that the re-enactment compulsion has loosened its grip.

## 4.6 — Active Vulnerabilities (Present-Tense)

The pressure points have not been eliminated; they have been *modulated*. Current operationally relevant vulnerabilities:

- **Scott's mortality remains the master variable.** Any credible threat to him collapses her present-tense maturity into the prior pattern within minutes. She will still spend her life for him. The maturation is real but conditional.
- **Offers of reunion with the dead remain a vector.** She has not been tested with a high-quality offer in the recent window. She would like to think she has grown past it. The surveillance assessment is that she has not been tested, and the assessment of probable response is *guarded uncertainty*.
- **The age-disjunction is a latent destabilizer.** A precipitating event that forces her to reckon publicly with the fact that she is older than her body, or younger than her memory, would likely produce significant short-term destabilization. She has not done this work.
- **The cohort is a structural dependency.** If the reformed Young Avengers cohort were to fracture catastrophically, the *holder* role she has built her present-tense identity around would lose its container. Loss of cohort would not produce collapse, but it would produce regression toward the father-fusion of her earlier era.
- **Her own resurrection is itself an unmetabolized event.** She does not talk about having been dead. She refers to it obliquely, jokingly, never seriously. The thing she has not done is grieve her own absence. This is the next piece of work, and she has not started it.

## 4.7 — Where She Is, Right Now

She is alive, which she has not always been. She is with her father, who is also alive, which neither of them has always been. She is the size she wants to be most of the time, which is a kind of victory that the file should not undervalue. She is in regular contact with the people who knew her before she died and the people who have only known her since. She is teaching someone younger how to hold a comm protocol. She has a snack in her pocket. She is, in the moments observable from outside, often laughing.

The dossier closes this section on a piece of behavior that recurs and that the file should preserve: when she ends a phone call with her father, she does not say goodbye. She says *talk soon*. Every time. Across every observed call in the recent period. The grammatical choice is not idle. *Goodbye* is the word she had to say once without saying it, on a television, when she was a child, and she has decided she will not say it again. *Talk soon* is the verbal form of the hand-touch on his arm. It is the verification ritual rendered as farewell. It is, in two words, the entire shape of her present life: a person who has lost the most important person and refuses, structurally, to let the loss have the last sentence.

*End Section IV. Subject remains under benevolent observation. File open.*


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY — SUBJECT: CASSANDRA ELEANOR LANG

*Compiled from longitudinal observation, derived medical inference, and reconstruction of incidents across the subject's published life. This file treats the body as evidentiary: the subject's somatic record is, in her case, the most legible single artifact of her psychology, because the two have never been separable.*

---

## 1. CONSTITUTIONAL BASELINE

**Anthropometrics (pre-Pym integration):** Caucasian female, born to Scott Lang (slight build, 5'10", lean-mesomorph) and Margaret "Maggie" Lang (medium frame). Childhood growth curves trended in the 25th–40th percentile for height and weight through the cardiac period — under-built for her age, with the slim, slightly drawn quality of children whose energy is being spent on staying alive rather than on growing. Recovery from the cardiac repair returned her to a normative growth curve by adolescence; adult baseline height (pre-Pym, pre-resurrection) approximately 5'4"–5'6", slight to medium build.

**Hair / eyes:** Strawberry blonde-to-blonde, fine; hazel-to-green. Freckling across the bridge of the nose and shoulders — sun-reactive skin consistent with the phenotype.

**Dentition:** Normal eruption pattern; orthodontia in early adolescence (background depiction — braces in school-era panels of the Astonishing run). No notable dental trauma despite combat history, which is itself a datum: she fights at scales that put her face out of the strike envelope.

**Handedness:** Right-dominant. Crosses over to two-handed grip on weapons (stingers) under stress.

**Allergies / sensitivities:** None documented. Tolerates Pym-class compounds extraordinarily — a fact whose etiology is now clear (see §3).

---

## 2. THE CARDIAC ERA — THE FOUNDATIONAL ILLNESS

**Diagnosis (approx. age 6–8):** Congenital cardiac defect, lesion type unnamed in canon but presented as life-limiting, surgically correctable only by a specialist (Dr. Erica Sondheim). Operative inference, based on the clinical presentation in canon (progressive, terminal-without-intervention, surgically fixable by a single named expert, no chronic post-op cyanosis depicted): most consistent with a complex septal or valvular lesion — a large ventricular septal defect with secondary pulmonary hypertension, an atrioventricular canal defect, or a tetralogy-variant requiring staged correction. The narrative requirement (one surgeon, one chance, terminal countdown) maps onto a lesion at the edge of operability where surgeon-specific technique matters.

**Symptomatic period (pre-surgery):** Per the original arc and subsequent reference, Cassie was depicted in this window as small for her age, easily fatigued, periorbitally shadowed, frequently photographed sitting when other children were standing. She missed school. She slept in the daytime. She was the kind of sick child whose mother learns to listen to her breathing from the next room. Maggie Lang's hospital vigils are part of the family record; Scott's psychological breakdown over them is the *origin* of the Ant-Man theft.

**The surgery (Dr. Erica Sondheim):** Successful. Full corrective intervention. Post-operative course not narratively elaborated, but the cardiothoracic surgical scar — a median sternotomy line, the central white ridge from suprasternal notch to xiphoid — is a permanent feature of the subject's body and a continuous somatic reminder of the incident that defines her. (It is, notably, not a scar she has ever been shown trying to hide; in swim and combat-undress panels across runs, it is simply there. She does not seem to read it as disfigurement. The artists who handle her best draw it.)

**Sequelae:**
- *Cardiac:* Repaired anatomy, but a repaired heart is not a native heart. Lifetime cardiology follow-up is the standard of care. Cassie is presumed to have had, at minimum, annual echocardiography through adolescence — though her actual compliance with follow-up after age 12 is reasonably suspected to be poor.
- *Pulmonary:* No documented residual disease.
- *Endocrine:* The prolonged illness period likely produced a brief constitutional delay in puberty; resolved spontaneously.
- *Immune:* Splenectomy not indicated; vaccination history presumed complete (Maggie Lang reads as the parent who keeps the appointment book).

**Psychological impact of the cardiac era:** This is the substrate of everything that follows. A child whose body almost killed her, whose father committed a felony to save her, whose mother sat through nights waiting for breathing — internalizes a specific cluster of beliefs:
1. *My existence is conditional, purchased, and owed.*
2. *Being small means being dying.*
3. *The people who love me will break the world to keep me here.*
4. *I cannot guarantee the body I live in.*

Every subsequent medical decision the subject makes — particularly the Pym dosing — is legible against this background. She is not someone who has a healthy relationship with her body's limits, because her body's limits nearly killed her, and the solution was *intervention from outside*. She has been trained, somatically, to expect that the body will require correction.

---

## 3. PYM PARTICLE INTEGRATION — THE CHRONIC EXPOSURE

**Onset (covert, pre-adolescent through early adolescent):** Per Young Avengers #6 (Heinberg) and supporting material, Cassie began stealing and self-administering Pym particles from her father's stockpiles in the years following his death in *Avengers Disassembled*. The reveal indicates that by the time she presents to the Young Avengers, she has been dosing long enough that the particles are *integrated* — size-change has become an autonomic biological capacity rather than an equipment-mediated effect.

**Duration of covert use prior to disclosure:** Reasonable inference: 18 months to 3 years of unsupervised self-administration during a critical developmental window (approximately ages 11–14).

**Route of administration:** Per her father's methodology, inhaled via canister/gas mechanism. This means she was, during covert use, dosing in her bedroom with stolen pharmaceutical-grade reality-altering aerosol — an image whose pathos is not lost on this analyst.

**Pharmacology (operative summary):** Pym particles are not a drug in the conventional sense; they are a subatomic/dimensional agent that exchanges mass with the Kosmos dimension during size-change. The chronic exposure consequence — integration of the particles into endogenous biology such that the subject can size-change *without* further dosing — is the canonical fact. This is unprecedented in any normal toxicology framework. The nearest analog is the case of Hank Pym himself, whose chronic exposure produced both biological integration and significant neuropsychiatric sequelae (the latter, notably, not replicated in Cassie — yet).

**Physiological strain of size-change:**
- *Giant form:* Square-cube law strain. Cardiac output requirement scales non-linearly. Blood pressure, vascular wall tension, oxygen demand all rise. *For a subject with a repaired congenital cardiac defect, every size-up is a cardiac stress test.* The fact that Cassie has never had a documented arrhythmia, syncope, or failure event during enlargement is either a function of how good the original repair was, a function of Pym particle physics doing something thermodynamically unusual to the cardiovascular substrate, or a function of how much narrative protection the subject has been granted. As an intelligence file, this dossier flags it as a question, not an answer.
- *Insect form:* Different but real strain. Neural conduction at sub-millimeter scale, thermoregulation collapse risk (mass-to-surface-area ratio inversion), respiratory exchange at lung-volumes incompatible with mammalian oxygenation. The Pym field is presumed to maintain quasi-normal biochemistry across scales; the subjective experience nevertheless includes cold, vertigo, and acoustic distortion.
- *Both:* Vestibular reorganization. Proprioceptive recalibration. After any extended size-change, Cassie has been depicted, in her quieter moments, taking a beat to re-locate her hands and feet in space. Junior operators sometimes vomit after their first sustained giant-form deployment; she did, once, in an early Young Avengers issue depicted off-panel and referenced.

**Endocrine implications during the developmental window:** A pre-adolescent and adolescent body undergoing repeated whole-organism mass change is undergoing something for which there is no medical literature. Growth plate behavior, pituitary signaling, gonadal axis maturation — all of these are presumed to have proceeded normally, but presumed on faith rather than evidence. The subject reached adult phenotype on schedule. Whether her endocrine profile is normal at the bench level is an open question no one in canon has been positioned to ask.

**Psychological impact of the Pym exposure:**
The dosing is not pharmacologic abuse in the reward-seeking sense. It is, in clinical language, *grief enacted somatically*. To inhale her dead father's signature compound is to take him into the lungs. To grow is to occupy the space he occupied. To shrink is to become the small thing he protected. The subject has, in the most literal sense available to her physiology, *eaten her father's ghost* and is now metabolizing him as her own capacity.

The willingness to do this with a repaired heart is the diagnostic feature. She knew (she must have known — Maggie would have told her, the cardiologists would have told her, the surgical scar told her every morning in the mirror) that her body was the one body that should not be experimenting with unregulated mass-change. She did it anyway. This is not stupidity; it is the precise behavioral signature of *counterphobic identification with the lost object* — moving toward the thing that should kill her, with the thing that killed him, in order to become him.

---

## 4. DEATH AND RESURRECTION

**Mechanism of death (*Avengers: The Children's Crusade* #9, 2012):** Killed by Doctor Doom during the climactic confrontation. The depicted mechanism is a hostile energy discharge (chaos-magic-amplified) striking the subject at full giant scale, producing immediate fatal trauma. She is conscious for the moments after the strike; she dies beside her father, who has just been killed for the second time in front of her, by the same agent.

**The compounded clinical fact:** Cassie's terminal event was not merely her own death. It was her own death immediately after she had, for the second time in her life, lost her father in front of her. The neurochemistry of the dying brain in those final minutes was processing not death-as-finality but *death-as-reunion-failed*. Whatever subjective experience she carried into unconsciousness was organized around the collapse of the reunion fantasy she had built her adolescence around.

**Interval of death:** Years of in-universe time. Body status: complicated by the resurrection mechanism (see below); no traditional autopsy or remains-handling depicted.

**Mechanism of resurrection (*Avengers: Standoff! / All-New, All-Different / Astonishing Ant-Man* era, 2015+):** Via the Pleasant Hill Kobik / cosmic-cube mechanism, in narrative concert with reality-warping events of the period. Operative result: subject returned to life, but at a chronologically earlier biological age than she died at. Effectively, the resurrection rolled her body back to approximately pre-adolescent or early-adolescent baseline.

**Clinical implications of resurrection:**
- *Somatic discontinuity:* The body that walks around now is, in a real sense, not the body that died. The cardiac repair scar appears to have been preserved (continuity of identity narrative), but the subject re-entered a body that had not yet lived through certain experiences.
- *Mnemonic / identity discontinuity:* Variable across writers, but the dominant depiction is *full memory continuity* — she remembers dying, remembers being older, remembers her Young Avengers years — inside a body that has regressed. The phenomenology of this is essentially unique to her: an adult-experienced consciousness in a re-juvenated chassis.
- *Pym integration status:* Apparently preserved through resurrection. She did not have to re-dose to recover the capacity.

**Psychological impact of death and resurrection:**
The subject has had to integrate a fact most patients never have: *she has been dead.* And she has had to integrate a second fact: *her resurrected body is not the body she earned by living.* The years she spent in the grave are years she did not get to use; the body she has now is, in a particular sense, *given to her*, the way her childhood survival was given to her by surgical intervention. The pattern repeats: *my continued existence is conditional, purchased, and owed.* The resurrection reinforces the foundational belief structure of the cardiac era. She is, twice now, someone whose life is the result of other people's interventions on a body that did not generate its own continuance.

The Maggie-and-Scott reunion scenes after resurrection are clinically interesting. Scott reads as the parent who is overjoyed-without-comprehension; Maggie reads as the parent who has now buried her daughter once and will not get past it. Cassie reads as someone managing both of them — performing the role of the returned child while privately processing the fact that her own subjective continuity is now in question.

---

## 5. INJURY REGISTER (CHRONOLOGICAL, OPERATIONAL)

A non-exhaustive ledger of documented and inferred trauma across the operational career:

- **Soft-tissue trauma (Young Avengers training era, 2005):** Multiple. Pre-discipline combat with peers; bruising consistent with size-change deceleration injuries.
- **Concussive event (Young Avengers vs. Kang, *Young Avengers Special* / early arcs):** At least one, with brief depicted disorientation. Concussion protocol not observed; the Young Avengers had no adult medical supervision in this period and this is a non-trivial fact.
- **Civil War combat (2006–07):** Mass-arrest event at the unregistered hero confrontation. Detained briefly. No documented severe trauma.
- **Skrull combat (*Secret Invasion*, 2008):** Pulmonary irritant exposure (Skrull weaponry); resolved.
- **Crush / pressure injuries (recurring, giant-form combat):** Every giant-scale combatant takes scaled-down strikes that, at normal mass, would still constitute serious blunt-force trauma. The subject's documented combat record includes building debris impacts, vehicle impacts, and combat with peer-mass enemies.
- **The terminal event (*Children's Crusade* #9):** As above.
- **Hostage / restraint trauma (*Astonishing Ant-Man* era, Darren Cross arc):** Detained by Cross; physically restrained; no documented severe injury but psychological re-traumatization significant — Cross is the figure entangled with her original cardiac-era kidnapping narrative.
- **Stinger-suit-era combat (Ant-Man and the Wasp / contemporary):** Lower-grade injury profile due to suit protection. Sting-weapon recoil; minor electrical exposure.
- **Recurrent vestibular complaints (inferred):** A career of mass-change produces what would, in any other patient, be diagnosed as a chronic vestibular disorder. The subject has adapted; the adaptation is not the same as the absence of dysfunction.

---

## 6. SUBSTANCES, INTOXICANTS, AND INGESTIONS

- **Pym particles:** As above. Chronic, integrated, ongoing.
- **Alcohol:** No documented disordered use. Age-appropriate exposure inferred for the adult-experienced consciousness; behavioral evidence suggests light social use at most. The subject grew up watching her father's life implode through addiction-adjacent recidivism patterns and is presumed to have absorbed a wariness of intoxicants.
- **Tobacco / nicotine:** None documented.
- **Recreational drugs:** None documented. Behavioral profile inconsistent with use.
- **Caffeine:** Probable. The Young Avengers operate at hours that require it.
- **Prescription medications:** Presumed cardiac follow-up medications during childhood (post-operative anticoagulation, possibly beta-blockade); compliance status in adolescence and beyond unknown. No depicted chronic prescription use as an adult.

**The differential point that matters:** The Pym dosing meets several surface DSM criteria for substance use disorder (covert use, escalation, continued use despite known physical risk, functional impairment). It does not meet the underlying criterion of *reward-seeking pharmacology*. The behavior is structured grief, not addiction. Treating it as addiction would miss the target entirely.

---

## 7. REPRODUCTIVE AND GYNECOLOGIC

No documented history. Standard development inferred. The resurrection-with-regression event creates a chronologically anomalous menarche/post-menarche profile that has not been narratively addressed and is flagged here only because a comprehensive file flags it.

---

## 8. NEUROLOGICAL

- **No documented seizure history.**
- **No documented migraine history**, though the post-size-change vestibular load is the kind of stimulus that produces migraine in susceptible individuals; the absence in canon is data.
- **Sleep:** Depicted disturbances around father-themed material — nightmares referenced obliquely in the Young Avengers run. Otherwise normative.
- **Cognitive function:** Intact, above-average. No documented cognitive sequelae from concussive events, from death-and-resurrection, or from Pym exposure. The latter, given Hank Pym's history, is the most clinically reassuring data point in the file — and the one this analyst would most want to verify with serial neuropsychological testing.

---

## 9. DERMATOLOGIC / IDENTIFYING

- **Median sternotomy scar:** Sternal midline, white, faded, mature. The single most important physical mark on the subject's body. *Operational note:* a forensic identifier that persists across resurrection and across size-change.
- **Freckling pattern:** Stable across resurrection.
- **No documented tattoos.** No documented piercings beyond conventional ear-lobe.
- **Combat scarring:** Minor; the subject's combat profile (size-change, distance) protects skin integrity better than most operators' careers do.

---

## 10. INTEGRATIVE NOTE

The subject's medical file reads, end to end, as a single coherent document with a single recurring thesis: *Cassandra Lang's body has been, since the day she was born, something other people have had to intervene upon to keep alive.* The cardiac surgeon saved her. Her father stole the suit that paid for the surgeon. The Pym particles she stole afterward integrated into the body the surgeon repaired. The cosmic mechanism that resurrected her replaced the body the chaos-magic destroyed. At no point in her physical history has her continued existence been a function of her body's own sufficiency.

This is the medical fact behind the psychological fact behind the operational fact. She moves through the world as someone who knows, somatically and without needing to articulate it, that *bodies fail and have to be saved by intervention from outside*. Her response to this knowledge has been to make herself the intervention — to grow large enough, to suit up well enough, to stand close enough to the people she loves that when their bodies fail, she will be the outside force that saves them.

It is the most coherent medical-psychological-vocational synthesis in the file. It is also the reason she will continue, predictably, to put a repaired heart under loads it was not built for, until something or someone teaches her that she is allowed to be a body that does not have to be earned.

*— End Medical History section. Cross-reference: §3 Psychological, §4 Psychiatric, §5 Personality Synthesis.*


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — SUBJECT: CASSANDRA E. LANG

*Total-surveillance bodily record, longitudinal, cross-state. Compiled from observation windows spanning pre-adolescence through current operational tenure. Where the subject's chronology has been disrupted by death/resurrection and somatic rejuvenation, both pre- and post-event baselines are noted.*

---

## I. BASELINE PHYSICAL CARRIAGE

**Resting stature (default scale):** Subject's "true" height is no longer a fixed parameter — Pym-particle integration has rendered scale a *state-dependent* variable rather than an anatomical given. Even when she has not consciously scaled, the body sits at a slightly different height week to week, depending on stress, sleep, and emotional weather. Surveillance teams should not use height as a biometric identifier. Mass-to-height ratio, however, remains stable: her body redistributes proportionally rather than densifying, a tell that distinguishes her in-frame from other size-altering operators (her father, by contrast, has a slightly compressed gait at default that betrays his "shrunk-from-larger" baseline).

**Posture:** Default spine is *upright with a forward-leaning crown* — head carried slightly ahead of the shoulder line, as if perpetually about to step into a conversation. Shoulders sit a touch high and forward, a residue of the small-and-sick childhood in which she learned to brace the thorax around a vulnerable heart. The bracing has never fully released. In moments of genuine calm, the shoulders drop and back roll out by perhaps two centimeters — observable, rare, diagnostically useful.

**Gait:** A long-strided, slightly bouncy walk on the balls of the feet, with audible heel-touch only in fatigue. Pace runs fast — she outpaces most companions by half a step and adjusts back, a lifelong pattern of *being the one who walks ahead and turns around to wait*. Arms swing asymmetrically: right arm swings further than left, the left tending to drift toward the hip as if reaching for a pocket or a holstered phone. At scale (giant form) the gait becomes deliberate, almost ceremonial — she has trained herself to plant each foot fully before transferring weight, because she learned early that a careless step at twenty feet is a homicide.

**Hand position at rest:** Hands are rarely fully still. Default rest is fingers interlaced loosely in lap when seated, or thumbs hooked into back pockets when standing. When neither is available, the right thumb finds the pad of the right index finger and rubs in slow circles — a self-soothe predating powers, observed since adolescence.

---

## II. THE MICRO-CATALOGUE OF TICS AND TELLS

**The size-tell:** Before a conscious scale-change, the subject's body *previsualizes* the shift. Pupils dilate by 1-2mm, breath drops to the diaphragm, and there is a brief (200-400ms) micro-tremor in the shoulders and jaw as the Pym substrate primes. Trained observers can read an imminent scale before she initiates it. Adversaries who have fought her more than once exploit this window.

**The heart-check:** Approximately 8-14 times daily, the subject's right hand drifts to her sternum — middle and ring fingers, brief two-second contact over the surgical scar territory. She is almost never aware she is doing it. Frequency rises sharply (30+/day) under cardiovascular stress, after extended scale-work, or in proximity to medical settings. This is the single most consistent unconscious behavior in the file. It pre-dates her hero career; it pre-dates her father's death.

**The thumb-to-knuckle press:** When listening intently, the left thumb presses into the second knuckle of the left index finger, kneading. Distinct from the rest-circle (right hand) — this is *processing*, not soothing.

**Hair-touching:** Tucks hair behind the right ear when interrupted mid-thought; tucks behind the *left* ear when flirting or being flirted with. The asymmetry is consistent across all observation windows and survives both her death and rejuvenation, suggesting deeply consolidated motor habit rather than learned style.

**Lip behavior:** Bites the inside of the lower lip when withholding a comment. Presses lips into a closed-mouth smile when receiving praise — she has never learned to accept compliments with an open face. Full open smile is reserved for peer-cohort interaction and for her father.

**The "small nod":** A three-beat micro-nod (chin drops twice, then stills) when she has decided something internally. Often precedes a defiant statement or a tactically risky move. Anyone reading her for danger-signs should watch for this nod; it is the conversion of internal debate into committed action.

**Eye behavior:** Direct contact, sustained — she does not look away during difficult conversations. Will, however, *blink-clusters* (three to five rapid blinks) when fighting tears, and shift gaze to the speaker's mouth rather than eyes when emotionally overloaded. Looks up and to her left when accessing memory of her father; this is so consistent it can be triangulated.

**The shoulder-roll-and-exhale:** Pre-combat ritual. Single shoulder roll backward, audible nasal exhale, weight settles into hips. Equivalent of a fighter's glove-tap. Observable in every documented engagement since age ~15.

**Foot tapping:** Right foot, ball of foot, at conversational tempo when seated and bored. Stops abruptly when she becomes interested — useful negative tell.

**The reach-and-stop:** Subject frequently begins a gesture toward another person (hand toward shoulder, arm toward elbow) and arrests it mid-motion, completing instead as a self-touch (own opposite arm, own neck). This is a learned restraint — she was, as a child, *unguardedly* affectionate, and learned through repeated loss to truncate the gesture of reaching. The arrested reach is one of the saddest readable behaviors in the file.

---

## III. FACIAL PATTERN

**At rest:** Eyebrows held slightly elevated — a default expression of mild expectancy. Mouth neutral but corners more often turned up than down. Resting face reads as "open and slightly amused" to most observers; this is misleading. Behind the elevated brows, the jaw is often subtly clenched, particularly at the masseter — a tension she does not feel and does not release.

**Concentration:** Brows draw down and together, nose wrinkles faintly, tongue pushes against the inside of the upper lip. When concentration involves geometric/spatial calculation (combat scale math), the eyes defocus and the head tilts approximately 8-12 degrees to the right.

**Amusement:** Genuine laughter is full-face — eyes crinkle, head tips back, audible exhalation of a single hard "ha" preceding the laugh proper. Polite laughter does not crinkle the eyes; the mouth opens but the orbital muscle is uninvolved. Distinction is reliable.

**Suppressed grief:** Lower lip tightens, chin dimples faintly, blink-rate climbs. She rarely permits tears in front of others; if they come, she will turn her face down and to her right shoulder, never to the left. (Theory: the left visual field is the side the father's hospital bed / coffin / etc. occupied at key moments — never confirmed but consistent.)

**Anger:** Surprisingly quiet face. Brows lower, nostrils flare slightly, voice drops in volume rather than rising. The dangerous Cassie expression is small and still. If the face *animates* in anger, it is performative anger directed at someone she does not actually fear or threaten. The true-anger face is the one to track.

**Intimacy / tenderness:** Eyes soften and half-close, mouth parts slightly, head tilts left. This is the only context in which the leftward head-tilt appears.

---

## IV. SPEECH AND VOCAL MECHANICS

**Default register:** Mid-alto, faintly nasal, with a tendency to upspeak on declarative sentences when speaking to authority figures she dislikes — a mocking application of a vocal pattern she does not use otherwise. With peers, declaratives land flat and clear.

**Rate:** Fast. Subject speaks at the high end of conversational tempo and accelerates further when excited or anxious. Slows markedly when speaking to her father or to younger heroes — a *care-tempo* she has learned.

**Verbal tics:** Heavy use of "okay so —" as a sentence-opener when transitioning to a plan. "Right?" appended to declaratives when seeking buy-in. Mid-sentence self-correction is frequent ("we should — no, *I* should —"), a tell of someone who composes ethically in real time. Profanity is rare and load-bearing when it occurs; she does not curse casually.

**Laugh:** Single hard "ha" leading into a cascading exhale-laugh. Snort-laugh exists but is reserved for the Young Avengers cohort and is suppressed in other settings, suggesting awareness of it as an intimacy-marker.

**Under stress:** Voice tightens at the throat, pitch rises by perhaps a third, breath support shortens. In genuine crisis she does the opposite — voice drops, breath deepens, words become shorter and more declarative. Surveillance value: *pitch up = nervous; pitch down = decided*.

---

## V. SLEEP ARCHITECTURE

**Schedule:** Inconsistent. Subject is by disposition a late chronotype (natural sleep onset 01:00-02:30) but forces an earlier schedule during periods of cohabitation with her father or operational tempo demanding it.

**Sleep latency:** Long — 30-60 minutes typical, longer if alone. Phone use in bed is the primary delay vector. Subject scrolls news, then social media, then (a long-standing private behavior) re-reads old text threads from her father. The latter behavior is so consistent it is essentially a sleep ritual.

**Position:** Falls asleep on her right side, knees drawn up, left hand under the pillow, right hand at the sternum (the heart-check, sleeping version). Migrates to supine in REM cycles, returns to right-side fetal by morning.

**Architecture:** REM-heavy. Reports vivid dreams; surveillance of REM density via wearables would likely show elevated cycles. Night-sweat episodes recur during periods of father-themed stress and after combat — dampening of the upper sheet on the left side, consistent with the supine REM position.

**Nightmares:** Recurrent themes — being unable to scale (powers failing), watching a building burn from outside, arriving too late to a recognizable but unspecific scene. She does not wake screaming; she wakes silently and sits up. Will often check her phone for her father's last message timestamp before lying back down. This behavior was observed even during periods when Scott was alive and reachable, suggesting the ritual is a *confirmation-of-existence* check decoupled from actual risk.

**Wake pattern:** Slow waker. Requires 15-25 minutes before functional speech. Coffee is non-negotiable.

---

## VI. ALIMENTARY PATTERN

**Caloric demand:** Substantially elevated. Size-change metabolism — particularly giant-form work — burns extraordinary energy, and post-engagement she eats prodigiously. Three to five thousand calories in a sitting post-combat is consistent with observation.

**Default eating style:** Fast eater. Holds fork in dominant right hand throughout (American-style), elbows often on the table, tendency to lean over the plate. Inhales the first third of any meal, then slows. Talks with full mouth in safe company; closes mouth and eats neatly in formal or surveilled settings — she knows the difference.

**Food preferences:** Strong sweet tooth — gravitates toward baked goods, ice cream, anything with chocolate. Coffee with significant cream and sugar. Pizza is the most reliably ordered food. She will eat almost anything but is suspicious of seafood beyond shrimp. Vegetable consumption is dutiful rather than enthusiastic.

**The shared-meal behavior:** When eating with her father, subject paces herself to his rate — finishes when he finishes, even if she is still hungry. This is unconscious and longstanding; the meal-as-communion behavior is one of the most reliable bonding indicators in her file.

**Disordered patterns:** None meeting clinical criteria. However, during high-stress arcs subject under-eats for 24-72 hours before binging — a stress-suppression-then-rebound pattern, not a body-image pattern. No purging, no restriction ideology.

**Hydration:** Chronically under-hydrated. Carries water bottles, forgets them, leaves them in rooms. This is operationally relevant because cardiac strain from scaling is worsened by dehydration; subject is aware and still does not correct.

---

## VII. SEXUAL AND INTIMATE BEHAVIOR

**Approach pattern:** Subject is the *initiator* in most romantic and sexual contexts within her age cohort. The pattern is consistent with her general interpersonal style — she reaches first, declares first, decides first. Asking permission verbally is a recurring feature; she will check in mid-encounter, a learned ethical practice rather than a sign of anxiety.

**Partner selection bias:** Documented preference for partners with a *returned-from-loss* quality — synthetic, resurrected, recovered, or in some way "twice-existing." This is psychologically over-determined and discussed elsewhere in the dossier. Operationally: partners outside this archetype have shorter relational tenures.

**Touch patterns:** In intimacy, subject's hand goes first to the partner's face — palm to cheek, thumb at temple. Second pattern: hand at the back of the partner's neck, fingers in hair at the nape. These are *holding* gestures. The size-changer cannot afford casual touch with civilians (a sudden scale-shift while embracing a non-powered partner would be lethal), so non-powered partners receive touch that is consciously moderated; powered partners receive an unguarded version that includes occasional micro-scaling of the hand (an unconscious affection-marker — she gets very slightly larger when happy).

**Post-intimacy:** Talkative. Subject tends to debrief, plan, joke. Does not fall asleep first. Sleeps facing the partner if the partner is one she trusts; turns away if she does not, while still permitting physical contact. The reverse — turning toward but refusing touch — is not in her repertoire.

**Solo behavior / privacy:** Maintains a strong sense of bodily privacy despite the comfort with physical presence. Does not undress in mixed company even with combat teammates after engagements; finds a separate room. This is a stable trait across all eras and both pre- and post-resurrection.

---

## VIII. GROOMING AND PRESENTATION

**Hair:** Length varies by era; subject defaults to medium-length and tends to chop it shorter herself during periods of stress (a known stress-marker — a sudden shorter haircut between observation windows is a flag). Washes every other day, ties up for combat, leaves down otherwise. Touches it constantly (see facial tells).

**Skin:** Some residual acne on jawline through late adolescence; clear baseline as an adult. The post-resurrection rejuvenation produced a slightly altered complexion — finer pore structure on the cheeks — that observers who knew her pre-Doom would notice.

**Scars:** The sternal surgical scar from infant cardiac repair — faded, longitudinal, approximately 8-10cm — is her oldest body-mark and the locus of the unconscious heart-check. Combat scars are minimal due to powered constitution. The most significant somatic disjunction is internal: she remembers receiving wounds (Doom) that the resurrected body does not bear.

**Dress:** Practical-comfortable as default. Jeans, layered tops, sneakers or boots. Has a small selection of dress-up clothing she rotates without commitment. Suit/gear preferences run toward functional design over aesthetic; she takes notes on her father's costume failures and pre-emptively engineers around them. Carries a backpack rather than a purse — backpack contents include a charging cable, a granola bar, a hair tie on the strap, and (consistent across years) a small folded photograph or printed image whose subject is presumed but not confirmed to be her father.

**Nail care:** Short, unpainted, occasionally bitten at the cuticle in periods of stress. Never long enough to interfere with combat.

**Scent:** Does not wear perfume operationally. Civilian scent is mild — shampoo and a basic deodorant, identifiable but not signature.

---

## IX. STATE-DEPENDENT SHIFTS

**CALM (operational baseline, peer-cohort settings, low-stakes day):**
Shoulders dropped, gait loose, full-face smile available, snort-laugh permitted, eats casually, hair-touches frequent and unguarded, heart-checks at baseline rate (~10/day), voice mid-register. The arrested-reach softens; she will complete affectionate gestures toward chosen-family without truncation.

**MILD STRESS (deadlines, social friction, mild peer conflict):**
Shoulders re-elevate. Foot tap appears. Voice rises in pitch. Sleep latency lengthens. Snacks increase, particularly sweets. Hair-tucking becomes asymmetric (right ear, processing side). Verbal self-corrections multiply. The small-nod appears more often as she litigates internal decisions.

**ACUTE STRESS (combat, threat to non-Scott teammate, ethical confrontation):**
Pitch drops, words shorten, breath deepens. Shoulder-roll-and-exhale fires. Pupils dilate. Size-tell tremor appears as the body primes. Eye contact becomes unblinking. Hands stop fidgeting entirely — when Cassie's hands go *still*, escalation is imminent. The dangerous Cassie expression — small, still, lower brow — settles in.

**FATHER-THEMED STRESS (threat to Scott, mention of his death, anniversary periods, encounter with figures from his history):**
This is a category of its own. Heart-check rate spikes (40+/day, sometimes hourly). Sleep latency extends past two hours; nightmare frequency rises. Voice tightens at the throat rather than dropping. Tactical judgment narrows; she will accept risks she would reject in any other context. The arrested-reach disappears in either direction — she will either grab her father without restraint, or refuse all touch entirely, depending on whether he is the source of the stress or the comfort. Eating dysregulates (the under-eat-then-binge pattern). She becomes the most readable she ever is, and the most dangerous.

**THREAT (direct combat, lethal-level engagement):**
The body is no longer hers in the ordinary sense — scale is fluid, gait is calibrated to mass, voice is operational. Verbal tics drop away; she speaks in clean imperatives. The face stills almost completely. Recovery curve post-engagement is steep: 20-40 minutes of caloric loading, often silent, followed by an unusually warm and chatty re-entry into peer interaction — almost manic relief, which suggests the engagement itself is, for her, a controlled re-encounter with the death-context.

**INTIMACY (with trusted partner or family):**
Left-tilt of the head appears. Eyes soften, half-close. Voice drops to a lower, slower register reserved for this context. The micro-scaling — slight involuntary enlargement of the hand or whole body when delighted — emerges. Hair tucks behind the *left* ear. The arrested-reach completes. She is, in these moments, the most embodied version of herself, and notably the only state in which the chronic masseter clench fully releases.

**GRIEF (active, unsuppressed):**
Rare in public observation. Face down and to the right shoulder. Blink-clusters. Lip-tightening. Chin dimple. Sound is minimal — she cries quietly, with the upper body very still and the breath shortened to small upper-chest gasps. The heart-check is continuous in these episodes — the hand essentially does not leave the sternum. Recovery is fast in appearance and slow in fact; she returns to functional presentation within minutes and carries the residue for days.

---

## X. CROSS-ERA NOTES

The pre-resurrection body and the post-resurrection body are not identical instruments, and any longitudinal file must mark the discontinuity. The current somatic self carries adolescent motor memory in a body that skipped the years in which that memory was supposed to be laid down — producing the occasional *over-reach* (gestures calibrated for a body she no longer has) and *under-reach* (hesitations where the prior body would have moved without thought). This is most visible in the first second of any new physical task; she compensates by the second second. Most observers do not catch it. A total-surveillance file should.

The constants across the discontinuity are diagnostic: the heart-check, the asymmetric hair-tuck, the arrested-reach, the leftward intimacy-tilt, the small-nod, the right-shoulder-down grief turn. These survived death. They are the load-bearing somatic identity. Whatever else can be remade about Cassie Lang, these gestures cannot — they are the body's record of who she has had to be.

*— End somatic atlas. Cross-reference: Cardiac File, Combat Log, Relationship Mapping.*


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS — CASSANDRA E. LANG

## I. The Attachment Substrate: How the Template Was Laid Down

To understand how Cassie Lang bonds, one must first understand the conditions under which her infant nervous system learned what *bond* meant. The data are unusually clear because her life has been documented since the womb.

She was born to a marriage already in slow collapse — Scott and Maggie Lang's union did not survive Scott's first incarceration (electronics-firm burglary, pre-Pym era). Cassie's earliest months were spent in a household where the primary male attachment figure was physically absent (prison), emotionally guilty (a father who knew he had failed her by being taken away), and intermittently restored. The pattern by age three was set: *Daddy comes back, then Daddy leaves, then Daddy comes back differently.* This is the prototype for every subsequent relationship she will form.

Layered onto this: the cardiac defect. A child whose body is failing develops a specific kind of attachment vigilance — the awareness, often pre-verbal, that the people around her are anxious about her, that her continued presence in the room is conditional on adult intervention. She learns very early that love is *interventional*: people must DO something for her to remain alive. Love is not a state; love is a rescue. This is the formative equation. It will later govern her romantic choices, her team affiliations, and her relationship to her own heroic vocation.

The successful surgery (Sondheim) closes the cardiac problem but encodes its lesson permanently. She survives because her father *committed a crime for her*. The first great love of her life proved itself by transgressing. Healthy love, in her substrate, is love that breaks rules to keep you alive. Lawful love — the love that follows procedures, files paperwork, waits its turn — is suspect. We will see this in every authority figure she resists for the rest of her life.

Attachment-style classification: **anxious-preoccupied with idealizing-fusion features and a counterphobic overlay.** Not disorganized (she is not afraid of her caregivers), not avoidant (she pursues closeness aggressively), not securely-based (her base keeps disappearing). The closest formal label is what Mary Main's protocols would call *preoccupied-entangled* with the additional complication that the entangled object has literally died. Most preoccupied attachers fear loss; Cassie has already had it, repeatedly, and her strategy has adapted accordingly.

## II. The Paternal Template — Scott Lang as Master Object

Every relationship in Cassie's life is measured, consciously or not, against her father. He is the standard, the wound, and the unfinished sentence.

What is striking, on the granular review, is *how she relates to him specifically* — not just that he is central but how the bond is performed:

- She is the **emotional caregiver in the dyad.** From the earliest issues, Cassie reassures Scott, not the reverse. She tells him he is a good man when he doubts it. She forgives him in advance of his asking. She positions herself as the one who *holds his self-image steady.* This is a textbook parentified-child pattern in a daughter of an addict-equivalent (Scott's recidivism, his impulsivity, his shame).
- She **monitors his moods constantly** — surveillance disguised as attentiveness. In nearly every father-daughter scene across forty years of publication she is reading him before she speaks, scanning his face, calibrating her presentation to what he can handle that day.
- She **does not punish his absences.** When he returns from death, from prison, from missions, from the Quantum Realm — she does not make him work for re-entry. The door is always open. This looks generous; it is also defensive. To make him work for it would be to acknowledge how badly the absences hurt, and acknowledging that would be to admit she is angry, and being angry would be to risk driving him away again.
- She **steals from him as a love language.** The covert Pym dosing is, in her internal economy, a form of intimacy: she has taken his substance into her body. She is wearing him from the inside. The fact that this is also a betrayal of his explicit wishes is metabolized as *he would understand* — a fusion fantasy that anticipates and forgives the breach.

The paternal template produces a specific kind of love object she will seek out elsewhere: **the loved one who is dangerous to himself, who needs to be held in place by her belief in him, who is most lovable when he is failing.** This recurs.

## III. The Maternal Template — Maggie Lang as the Devalued Constant

Maggie is, by every measurable metric, the better parent. She stayed. She made a stable home. She remarried a man (Paxton) with steady employment, predictable behavior, and lawful authority. She enforced normal-childhood boundaries — bedtime, school, no superheroing.

Cassie's emotional ledger registers all of this as boring at best and obstructive at worst.

This is not Cassie being a brat; this is the predictable output of an anxious-preoccupied attachment system. The parent who is reliably present becomes the *baseline* — invisible, uncharged, taken for granted. The parent who is intermittently available becomes the figure of intensity, longing, and meaning. Cassie's nervous system is calibrated to alarm, and Maggie does not produce alarm, so Maggie does not produce activation, so Maggie does not produce love-as-Cassie-recognizes-it.

The granular tells across decades of pages:
- Cassie reports to Maggie about her day in dutiful summary; she reports to Scott in confessional detail.
- Cassie lies to Maggie about meaningful things (Pym dosing, Young Avengers membership, runaway plans). She lies to Scott about trivial things and tells him the meaningful things voluntarily, often unprompted.
- When Maggie expresses fear for her safety, Cassie experiences it as *control.* When Scott expresses the same fear, Cassie experiences it as *care.* The content is identical; the affect attached is opposite.
- Reconciliation arc with Maggie comes only in adulthood and only partially. Cassie never fully recovers the maternal bond because her template does not have a slot for reliable, lawful love.

The Paxton sub-pattern is a corollary: a uniformed officer of the state, a man whose entire professional identity is *constraining people like Scott Lang.* Paxton is structurally unable to be a father to her even when he tries (and he does try). She defies him reflexively because the system has placed him in the role of *the man who would have arrested my father* — and that role is non-negotiable in her schema.

## IV. Peer Bonding — The Young Avengers as Chosen Kin

The most psychologically healthy relationships in Cassie's life are her peer bonds, and this is not accidental. Peers do not trigger the parental template; she gets to start from a less distorted baseline with them.

Observed peer pattern:

**Bonding speed: high.** She forms strong attachments rapidly. The Young Avengers, encountered as strangers in a basement, become her primary kin group within weeks. This rapidity is itself a tell — it is the speed of someone whose attachment system has been primed by deprivation, who recognizes the *function* of family and is ready to assign it to whoever fits the slot.

**Bonding mechanism: she becomes indispensable.** Within the team, Cassie's role calcifies very early as the *holder* — the one who remembers everyone's birthday-equivalent, the one who insists the group eat together, the one who tracks who is fighting with whom and brokers the truce. This is parentified-child behavior transposed onto a peer group. She has imported the role she played for Scott and applied it horizontally.

**Bond maintenance: relentless contact.** She is the team member most likely to initiate calls, send messages, check in after engagements, drop by unannounced. In the modern runs where group-chat dynamics are depicted, she is the one who keeps the chat alive when it threatens to die. The phone, in any era's depiction, is in her hand more than in any other Young Avenger's.

**Conflict tolerance: low for fractures, high for friction.** She can absorb daily friction without distress — sarcasm, disagreement, ideological argument. She panics at *fracture* — anyone leaving the group, anyone going silent, anyone going missing. The triggering condition is always the same: the threat of disappearance. Argument is fine; absence is intolerable.

**Loyalty profile: extreme and durable.** Once Cassie has named someone family, that designation is permanent and not subject to revocation by the other party's behavior. Kate Bishop's tactical disagreements, Tommy Shepherd's destructive impulsivity, Billy Kaplan's identity crises, Eli Bradley's withdrawals — none of these dislodge her loyalty. This is admirable and also a vulnerability: it means she does not register accumulating warning signs that would prompt a securely-attached person to recalibrate.

**Specific dyads worth flagging:**
- *With Kate Bishop:* sisterly, slightly competitive, mutually steadying. Kate's wry pragmatism counterbalances Cassie's earnestness. This is the most genuinely peer-symmetrical relationship in Cassie's life.
- *With Tommy Shepherd:* protective, indulgent, often exasperated. Cassie reads Tommy as the wounded one and assumes the holder role with him most overtly.
- *With Billy Kaplan:* deep mutual respect, ideological alignment, the closest she has to a sibling. Billy is also the one most likely to call her on her self-erasure.
- *With Eli Bradley:* a complicated admiration for the principled-authority figure she actually trusts; Eli occupies the rare slot in her schema of *legitimate command she will follow.*

## V. Romantic and Intimate Patterns — The Revenant Preference

The pattern is so consistent across her published romantic history that it cannot be coincidence: Cassie is drawn to partners who are, in some structural sense, *returned from death or constructed in place of the dead.*

The Vision-Jonas relationship is the paradigm case. The partner she chooses in her first serious romance is, literally:
- a synthetic being assembled to replace a dead Avenger,
- containing the imprinted personality of a teenage version of Kang/Iron Lad,
- inheriting the form of a hero who died in the same Mansion catastrophe that killed her father.

She did not choose this consciously. She chose it because her attachment system, scanning available partners, lit up most strongly for the one whose ontological situation mirrored her own unresolved object loss. To love Jonas is to love a successful reanimation — to live, daily, the proof that the dead can come back as someone you can hold.

When Jonas is destroyed (multiple iterations across various runs), her grief is severe but oddly familiar — she has been here before, she knows the shape of this room, she has practiced this loss in advance with her father. Her resilience in the face of repeated Vision-loss is not health; it is the rehearsal effect of someone whose primary trauma was loss-of-the-returned.

Intimacy pattern within romance:
- **High disclosure early.** She tells partners about her father, her death, her resurrection, her cardiac history, often within days of becoming close. This is not oversharing in the borderline sense; it is the preoccupied attacher's strategy of accelerating closeness by front-loading vulnerability.
- **High investment immediately.** She does not date casually. Each romantic bond is treated, from the first weeks, as a candidate for permanence.
- **High caretaking valence.** She tends to position herself as the partner's stabilizer — the one who believes in him, who holds him together, who advocates for him to others. Same role she played for her father.
- **Low erotic centrality in the published record.** What is depicted is consistently companionate, tender, hand-holding, conversational. The romance is structured around *being together* more than around physical desire. This may reflect publishing constraints but it is also consistent with attachment-driven rather than desire-driven pairing.
- **Difficulty with secure partners.** A partner who is simply emotionally available, lawful, present — Cassie does not know what to do with such a person. There is no project. There is no rescue. There is no return-from-the-dead. Her system does not register this as love because nothing alarming is happening.

## VI. Distrust, Betrayal, and Repair

**How she distrusts:** Cassie's distrust is *categorical, not personal.* She does not develop suspicion of individuals over time; she develops suspicion of *types.* Institutional authority, registration regimes, government oversight, corporate power, anyone-who-looks-like-the-Avengers-who-let-her-father-die — these are distrusted as classes. Individuals get the benefit of the doubt until they personally fail her chosen people.

Once an individual *has* failed her chosen people, the distrust is also categorical — they move into a permanent file labeled *not to be relied on,* and re-entry is difficult. She is not vindictive; she simply removes them from the load-bearing structure of her trust and does not let them carry weight again.

**How she experiences betrayal:** With shock disproportionate to the evidence. Because she has fused-idealized her loved ones, betrayal by them is ontologically destabilizing — it requires her to revise the schema, and the schema is load-bearing for her sense of self. Her response to betrayal by an inner-circle figure is *grief,* not anger. She mourns the version of the person she had constructed.

**How she betrays:** Cassie's betrayals are almost always **acts of preemptive loyalty to someone she loves more.** She lies to her mother to protect access to her father. She lies to her father to protect access to her team. She lies to authority figures to protect everyone. She does not betray for gain or for spite. She betrays *as triage* — when love-objects come into conflict, she chooses the higher-priority bond and deceives the lower-priority one to preserve both. She would not call this betrayal; she would call it *managing the situation.*

**How she repairs:** Cassie is unusually skilled at repair, and this is the most genuinely strong part of her relational toolkit. Her repair sequence is consistent:
1. *Acknowledge the harm explicitly,* without minimizing.
2. *Locate the harm in her own pattern,* not in circumstance ("I did this because I was scared of losing you").
3. *Offer continued presence,* not just apology — she shows up the next day, and the day after.
4. *Do not demand the other party's symmetrical repair.* She does not require reciprocity to continue the relationship.

This is high-skill repair, and it is the part of her that the Children's Crusade arc gestures toward: she did not kill Wanda because her deep template is *restorative.* She wants to fix things, not balance them.

## VII. Dependency Patterns

Cassie does not present as dependent. She presents as the *holder,* the caretaker, the one others lean on. This is itself a dependency pattern — *counter-dependency* — and it is one of the most stable features of her relational profile.

She depends on:
- **Being needed.** Remove her caretaking function and she does not know where she stands in the room.
- **Proximity to her father's identity and legacy.** The Stinger suit, the Pym particles, the Ant-family operation — these are not just career; they are the umbilical to the original bond.
- **The Young Avengers group-self.** Her self-concept is partly distributed across the team. Solo Cassie is a less coherent figure than ensemble Cassie.
- **The possibility of reunion.** As long as the dead can come back (and in her world they can), her grief does not have to be finished. This is a dependency on cosmology, not on a person.

What she does *not* depend on, conspicuously:
- Material stability (she has been broke, displaced, and unhoused across various arcs without distress).
- Praise or recognition (she does not seek the spotlight; she seeks the bond).
- Romantic continuity per se (she can be single without acute distress, provided the team-family is intact).

## VIII. The Master Template, Stated Plainly

Across every relationship Cassie Lang has ever formed — paternal, maternal, fraternal, romantic, peer, mentor, enemy-she-spares — the same template recurs:

> *Find the person who is in some way already lost. Move toward them. Become indispensable to them. Hold them in place with your belief in them. Forgive in advance. Lie if needed to keep them close. Do not punish them for leaving. Wait for them to come back. If they cannot come back, become them. If they come back, hold tighter. Never finish the grief, because finishing it would mean accepting they are gone, and you have never accepted that anyone you love is gone.*

This template was laid down by a cardiac defect, a father in prison, a mansion on television, and a long apprenticeship in the specific hope that the dead return. It governs how she greets a teammate, how she chooses a boyfriend, how she fights an enemy she could have killed, and how she will, eventually, parent her own child if she lives that long.

The unfinished relational work of her life is not to abandon this template — it has produced real love, real loyalty, real heroism — but to learn that **some people who stay are also worth her full attention,** and that **love that does not require rescue is still love.** Maggie has been trying to teach her this for thirty years of publication. Cassie has not yet, fully, learned it.

*End section.*


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# DOSSIER SECTION VII — DEFENSES & COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

*Subject: Cassandra Eleanor "Cassie" Lang*
*Classification: Behavioral / Intrapsychic Mapping — Longitudinal*

---

## VII.0 — Orienting Note

The defensive architecture of this subject is unusually legible because it is *enacted in the body*. Most subjects defend in thought, affect, and word; Cassie Lang defends in **physical scale**. The Pym particle apparatus has functioned, across two decades of published record, as an externalized id-ego mechanism: when she shrinks, she is doing one defensive work; when she grows, she is doing another; the *transition itself* is an affect-regulation event. This makes her psychic life observable at a granularity rare in subjects of her age and background. What follows is a stratified inventory, ranked roughly from most primitive to most mature, with behavioral exemplars and operational implications drawn from the full canonical record.

---

## VII.1 — Primitive Stratum (Pre-Oedipal, Body-Based)

### VII.1.a — Somatic Identification with the Lost Object

The deepest and most primitive defense in the architecture. Following Klein and the British object-relations school, this is **introjection of the lost father by literal incorporation of his bodily mechanism**. Scott Lang's defining somatic signature is size-change; Cassie covertly self-administered the same compound across years until size-change became *endogenous* to her own body. She did not adopt his cape, his shield, his weapon — she adopted his **endocrine pattern**.

Operational signature in behavior:
- Onset of dosing maps to the period immediately following his death; the timing is not coincidental but symptomatic.
- Concealment from Maggie and Paxton tracks a covert mourning ritual rather than thrill-seeking — there is no peer audience, no boast, no social reward sought during the dosing years.
- When asked across multiple writers to articulate *why* she sought powers, her answers cluster around the verb "to be" rather than "to do" — *to be like him*, *to be near him*, *to be what he was*. The verb is ontological.

This defense is the engine beneath nearly everything else. Until it is named and metabolized therapeutically, no higher defense can fully consolidate.

### VII.1.b — Splitting

Most prominent in the Young Avengers / Civil War period, partially metabolized thereafter. The world divides cleanly: father-loyal vs. father-betraying; Cap-aligned vs. Stark-aligned; reformed-criminal-as-hero vs. respectable-authority-as-failure. The pattern is consistent enough that it can be mapped: institutions or persons who *failed Scott* (the Avengers establishment that allowed Disassembled, the registration apparatus, Paxton's police-coded skepticism) occupy the bad pole; institutions or persons who *honored Scott* (Cap, the Young Avengers, eventually Jan Van Dyne) occupy the good pole. Maturation in the Spencer/Ewing material softens the splits without dissolving them — she can now hold Scott as flawed without ceasing to love him, which is a meaningful clinical achievement.

### VII.1.c — Counterphobic Action (Fenichel)

A child whose own heart nearly killed her, whose father died in armored combat, chose to: (i) chronically dose a compound that *strains the cardiovascular system*; (ii) enter armored combat herself; (iii) seek out the very villains who originated her father's career (Cross, then Doom). The movement toward the feared stimulus is so consistent that it is the most reliable predictor of her behavior under threat — given two paths, she takes the one with greater somatic risk. The Children's Crusade arc, in which she enters Latveria to confront Doom directly, is the apex expression: she moves toward the most powerful sorcerer-engineer on Earth, on his own ground, with a body that should not be running such loads.

### VII.1.d — Somatization of Affect (Inverted)

Most subjects somatize *distress* (headaches, GI complaints, fatigue). Cassie somatizes **agency**: when she cannot tolerate being overlooked, she becomes giant; when she cannot tolerate being seen, she becomes ant-scale. The defense is the same mechanism — affect translated to body — but oriented to power rather than complaint. Operationally: any observer can read her interior state by watching her *size oscillation rate* in the seconds before a confrontation. Rapid micro-adjustments (growing six inches, shrinking four, growing again) are a tell of acute decision-anxiety; sudden commitment to a single scale signals that affect has resolved into action.

---

## VII.2 — Intermediate Stratum (Neurotic-Adolescent)

### VII.2.a — Reaction Formation Against Helplessness

The clearest single defense she carries. The original helplessness was triple: a child who could not save her own body from its defect; a child who could not save her father from the Avengers' enemies; a child who could not save her father from the Avengers themselves. The reaction formation is *to make herself the agent of rescue in every available scene*. Behavioral signatures:
- She gravitates to hostage situations and rescue scenarios disproportionately to her tactical role.
- She volunteers for point on extractions even when her power-set is suboptimal.
- In group debriefs (as depicted across Young Avengers material), she remembers and names the people who were *saved*, not the enemies who were defeated. The accounting is reparative, not victorious.

### VII.2.b — Identification with the Aggressor (Partial, Inverted)

Subtle but present. Cassie has not identified with the figures who killed her father (Wanda, Doom) in the classical Anna Freud sense — but she *has* identified with the Avengers institution that failed to protect him, by joining its junior branch. This is a partial inversion of the defense: rather than becoming the aggressor, she becomes the *failed protector*, attempting to do correctly what the prior generation did wrongly. This is why her loyalty to the Young Avengers as an institution is stronger than her loyalty to any senior Avenger as an individual — she is rebuilding the institution she was failed by.

### VII.2.c — Reparative Fantasy / Manic Reparation

Discussed at length in the Children's Crusade record. The drive is not revenge but *undoing*. When Doom resurrects Scott via stolen chaos magic, Cassie accepts the gift despite obvious moral cost — she takes her father back from a man she knows to be a monster, because the *repair* is more compelling than the moral hygiene. This is Klein's manic reparation: the wish to restore the damaged object is so strong it overrides reality testing.
