*The asset ledger. What this subject has, what she can do, what she can take, and what about her endures. Compiled with the same granularity as the threat profile; an honest accounting requires both.*

---

## 7.1 PHYSICAL & BIOLOGICAL ASSETS

### 7.1.1 The Size-Change Capability — Itemized

The Pym particle integration is, on the asset side, one of the most operationally versatile powers in the active hero population. A full inventory:

- **Endogenous, equipment-independent operation.** Unlike her father and unlike Hank Pym in most configurations, Cassie's size-change is biological. She cannot be defeated by suit-tampering, helmet removal, regulator failure, or EMP. The asset is *internal*; it travels with her body across capture, undress, water immersion, and tech-null environments. This is a redundancy her father does not possess and operationally distinguishes her from the Ant-Man lineage.
- **Continuous-spectrum scaling.** Observed range across published material: insect-scale (~½ inch, comparable to Ant-Man baseline) through giant-scale (60+ feet, with occasional excursions higher). Crucially she scales *continuously* rather than in discrete jumps, which gives her tactical sizing — a doorway, a vehicle interior, a crowd's sightline — without coarse over- or under-shoot.
- **Mass-and-force conservation favorable to her.** When giant, she retains striking force commensurate with apparent size; when small, she retains baseline-human muscle output (or close to it) in a body that presents a fraction of the targetable surface area. Both poles are weaponized.
- **Real-time geometric cognition.** Size-change at speed in a three-dimensional combat environment requires constant calculation of reach, footing, momentum, allied positioning, and collateral risk. She does this fluently. This is a genuine cognitive skill, not a power; it indicates strong spatial intelligence and working-memory load tolerance.
- **Affect-regulation utility.** Documented in §5: when overwhelmed she scales up. This is a self-soothing somatic strategy with real benefits — it interrupts freeze responses, projects confidence she may not feel, and forces interlocutors to recalibrate. Most operators do not have a power that doubles as a panic-disorder intervention.

### 7.1.2 Cardiovascular Adaptation

Counterintuitive but documentable: a child with a repaired congenital heart defect who has nonetheless tolerated years of chronic Pym dosing without cardiac decompensation has, by selection, demonstrated unusual cardiovascular adaptability. The heart that almost killed her has been progressively stress-conditioned. This is not endorsement of the regimen — see §2 — but as an asset accounting, she has a cardiac system that has survived sustained extraordinary load. That is durability.

### 7.1.3 Post-Resurrection Vitality

Whatever the precise mechanism of her restoration (Pleasant Hill, Kang-adjacent manipulations, magical/cosmic synthesis), the resurrected body presents no documented chronic sequelae: no neurological deficit, no immune deficit, no shortened endurance. She came back functional. Many resurrected characters in this milieu do not.

### 7.1.4 Combat Conditioning

She has logged operational hours since adolescence. Reflexes, pain tolerance, recovery from concussive events, comfort with falling/being thrown, and the unflinching production of force against adult opponents are all present and trained. She has been hit by Doom-tier threats and continued to function until killed; her threshold is high.

---

## 7.2 COGNITIVE & TEMPERAMENTAL ASSETS

### 7.2.1 Verbal Fluency and Social Intelligence

Across every writer's hand, Cassie is depicted as articulate, quick, and capable of reading a room. She talks her way into the Young Avengers; she talks down peers in conflict; she negotiates with Captain America at fifteen without losing her footing. The asset: she can hold her ground in conversation with people decades her senior and several power-tiers above her, and she does it without strident affect. This is rare in adolescent operators.

### 7.2.2 Moral Reasoning Capacity

The Children's Crusade decision — not killing Wanda when she had cause, motive, opportunity, and team permission — is the diagnostic asset incident. She performed live ethical reasoning under maximum personal grief load and arrived at a restorative answer. Most adults cannot do this. Most heroes do not. This indicates a moral processing apparatus that operates *upstream* of grief rather than being captured by it.

### 7.2.3 Capacity for Forgiveness

Distinct from moral reasoning. Forgiveness is the affective release that follows the ethical decision; many people make the right call and continue to hate. Cassie demonstrably can both decide and *let go*. She has functional working relationships with figures who killed her father (Wanda, eventually), the regime that failed him, and the institutional Avengers that consumed him. This is not naivety — it is a deliberate, repeatedly-chosen disposition. As an asset it makes her *coalitionable*: she does not carry grudge-debt that prevents alliance.

### 7.2.4 Behavioral Processing Style

§3 notes she metabolizes through action rather than rumination. As an asset, this means: she does not get stuck. She does not spiral inward for weeks. Pain enters her system and is converted to movement — training, mission, reconciliation, gesture. The conversion is sometimes risky (see §5: re-enactment) but the underlying capacity — that affect *moves* through her rather than calcifying — is a major resilience factor and the reason a person with her loss history is functional at all.

### 7.2.5 Humor

Observable across runs and tone-stable across writers: dry, self-aware, generous (humor *with* people, rarely *at* them), used to defuse rather than dominate. Humor in someone with her history is not decoration; it is evidence of intact playfulness, intact hope, and a working theory-of-mind for what other people find funny — which requires being interested in other people. She is.

### 7.2.6 Idealism That Has Survived Disillusionment

She has had her father killed by the institution he idolized, been killed herself by a despot, been resurrected as a child, watched the world she fought for ratify increasingly authoritarian regimes — and remains idealistic. This is not innocence; it is *load-tested* idealism, which is a much rarer and more durable asset. Idealists who have never been hurt are brittle. Cassie's has been hammered and held.

---

## 7.3 RELATIONAL & SOCIAL CAPITAL

### 7.3.1 The Young Avengers Cohort

Her single most valuable durable asset. This is not a team in the operational sense; it is a chosen-kin network of peers who have collectively survived multiple crisis arcs, the death and return of members (including hers), romantic permutations within the cohort, and identity reformations. They function as her secondary attachment system and as a real-time reality check on her father-themed reactivity. Specific assets within the cohort:

- **Kate Bishop** — peer of comparable maturity and the cohort's other adult-in-the-room. Holds Cassie accountable without authority-coding. The friendship reads as primary.
- **Wiccan / Billy Kaplan** — magical heavy and the architect of the Children's Crusade. Shares with Cassie the experience of grief-driven quest behavior and the maturation that follows.
- **Hulkling / Teddy Altman** — stable presence, models a settled romantic life.
- **Vision-Jonas / subsequent iterations** — her romantic history within the cohort. Even where this relationship is fraught (§5, §3), it is *internal* to the kin network rather than alienating her from it.
- **Speed, Patriot, and subsequent additions** — depth of bench; she is not load-bearing for any single relationship.

The asset is structural: she has a peer group that does not need her to be Scott Lang's daughter, has known her through her worst arcs, and has both the will and the means to come for her if she is taken.

### 7.3.2 The Father

Mortality issues notwithstanding, when alive Scott Lang is an unambiguous asset: loving, present, will commit any crime necessary on her behalf, professionally competent, networked with the broader Avengers establishment, and increasingly willing to treat her as a peer operator rather than a child to be protected. The Astonishing run depicts him giving her the Stinger suit — a formal investiture that reframes the relationship from "daughter to be saved" toward "colleague."

### 7.3.3 The Mother and Stepfather

Underrated. Maggie Lang is the parent who stayed; Jim Paxton is a law-enforcement professional who provided structural stability across Scott's absences (incarceration, missions, deaths). Cassie's emotional economy may devalue them (§3) but the *operational* value is real: she had a stable home, regular meals, schooling, and a non-criminal address throughout childhood. The base-rate stability she takes for granted is what allowed her to survive Scott's instability. As an adult asset, Maggie and Paxton remain a safe house, a place to disappear to, and a non-cape support system that no enemy of her hero identity will think to monitor closely.

### 7.3.4 The Avengers Establishment (Tertiary)

Despite institutional grievances, Cassie has standing access to senior Avengers — her father's old colleagues regard her with protective affection (Jessica Jones, Hawkeye/Clint, the broader Avengers/West Coast network). She can call in favors at a tier most operators her age cannot reach.

### 7.3.5 The Pym Lineage

She is, in effect, the inheritor of a scientific dynasty — Hank Pym, Janet van Dyne, Scott, herself, and Nadia. This is a network of mentors, technical resources, and shared specialized knowledge. She is not the only person in the world who knows what it feels like to be six inches tall; that community, however small, is hers.

---

## 7.4 RESOURCE & MATERIEL ASSETS

- **Stinger suit / equipment cache** — formally issued by Scott; integrates with her endogenous size-change rather than substituting for it. Provides comms, environmental sealing, and offensive options.
- **Pym particle supply chain** — through her father, the Pym estate, and her own demonstrated capacity to synthesize/acquire. She is not dependent on a single source.
- **Avengers facility access** — variable by run and political moment but generally extant.
- **Young Avengers mobility** — through Wiccan's reality manipulation and Hulkling's interstellar standing, she has access to transport and exfiltration options exceeding her individual means.
- **Civilian identity intact** — she has retained a legal identity, family address, and social fabric throughout her career. Many operators have not.

---

## 7.5 RESILIENCE FACTORS — THE DURABILITY ANALYSIS

What makes the above *hold* under stress.

### 7.5.1 Coherent Self-Narrative

Even where her self-concept is contested (§3's two-pole problem), she has a *narrative*. She knows who she is, where she came from, what she is for, and why she fights. Operators without coherent self-narrative tend to break under sustained ideological pressure; she does not. The Civil War arc demonstrates this — placed in a position of having to choose between her father's old colleagues across a moral fault line, she chose, stayed chosen, and did not unravel.

### 7.5.2 Trauma That Is Located Rather Than Diffuse

Her wounds are specific, nameable, and bounded (§4). She is not free-floatingly anxious; she is grief-organized around identifiable events and triggers. This is a resilience asset because *located* trauma is workable trauma — it can be predicted, prepared for, and treated. Diffuse trauma cannot.

### 7.5.3 Pre-Trauma Baseline of Secure Attachment

Critical and underappreciated. Before Avengers Disassembled, Cassie had a father who loved her enough to commit felonies for her survival, and a mother who provided a stable home. The wound came down on a foundation of being loved. This is the single most reliable predictor of post-traumatic resilience in the developmental psychology literature, and she has it. Children who lose loving parents grieve and continue; children who never had them often cannot construct adult attachment at all. She had the foundation. The grief is severe but the substrate is intact.

### 7.5.4 The "Behavioral Processor" Architecture

Re-cited from §7.2.4 because it is doing double work as resilience: pain that moves does not pool.

### 7.5.5 Peer Group That Has Already Survived Her Death

The Young Avengers' relational glue includes the experience of losing her in Children's Crusade and getting her back. This means the network has *practiced* the worst-case loss with respect to her and continued. As resilience, this is enormous — her support system is post-tested.

### 7.5.6 Identity Capacity Independent of Powers

She has had her body change (resurrected younger), her abilities calibrated and re-calibrated, her costume changed, her name changed (Stature → Stinger → others), and remained recognizably herself across all of it. The Cassie underneath the configurations is durable. This is an asset many cape-identified operators lack — they are their suit; she is not.

### 7.5.7 Capacity to Be Wrong

She has reconciled with her father's moral ambiguity (§1's contemporary runs) — i.e., she has updated her idealized model of Scott in light of evidence and not collapsed. The ability to revise idealized internal objects without abandoning them is sophisticated psychological work, and it makes her *teachable* by experience. She gets better.

### 7.5.8 The Loss-Acceptance Increment

Across the long arc, each loss of Scott has been metabolized faster than the last. The first death produced a years-long psychological project (Young Avengers, Children's Crusade). Subsequent disruptions are absorbed more efficiently. The grief machinery is becoming more efficient even as the wound remains. Resilience here is not the absence of pain but the increasing throughput of it.

### 7.5.9 The Restorative Worldview

Her moral preference for repair over revenge is *itself* a resilience factor because revenge-organized psychologies are exhausting and tend to consume their host. Restoration is generative. It gives her something to build toward rather than something to destroy, which means her motivational engine does not burn out when targets are unavailable.

### 7.5.10 The "Held" Quality

A pattern worth naming explicitly: in nearly every group setting Cassie ends up doing emotional load-bearing for others — remembering birthdays, insisting on the team meal, calling the absent member, organizing the memorial. The asset is dual. First, this is a real skill and a real contribution to group function. Second, the *practice* of holding others is, paradoxically, what holds her — purpose-providing, attention-directing, and identity-confirming. She is most stable when she is being useful to people she loves. Her resilience is partly relational rather than purely individual, which means it is *renewable* — every act of holding others tops it back up.

---

## 7.6 META-ASSETS — WHAT THE ABOVE COMBINES INTO

Two emergent properties worth naming separately because they exceed the sum of their components.

### 7.6.1 Coalition Value

Combining forgiveness capacity (§7.2.3), the Young Avengers network (§7.3.1), the Avengers tertiary access (§7.3.4), and her coherent moral compass (§7.2.2): Cassie is one of the very few operators in her cohort who can plausibly call together a cross-generational, cross-faction working group on short notice and have it hold. She is a connective tissue character — politically, generationally, and emotionally. In a milieu defined by schisms, this is rare and operationally enormous.

### 7.6.2 Generational Bridge Function

She is the bridge between the Avengers original generation (her father's peers), the Young Avengers, and whatever comes after. She has the standing to be heard by the seniors and the trust to be followed by the juniors. This positions her as a *succession asset* for the heroic community as a whole — not just a powerful operator but a load-bearing node in the institution's continuity.

---

## 7.7 SUMMARY LEDGER

The fundamental finding of this section: Cassandra Lang's asset profile is unusually *integrated*. Her power, her psychology, her relationships, and her resilience factors are not independent line items — they reinforce each other. The size-change is also affect regulation. The grief-organized identity is also moral motivation. The peer group is also post-loss-tested support system. The forgiveness capacity is also coalition value. The behavioral-processor temperament is also resilience throughput.

This is the architecture of a person who, on the evidence of the published record, has more than survived what was done to her. She has converted it into the load-bearing structure of a functional adult heroic life — and the conversion is still happening. The asset side of this file grows with time. The threat side does not, at the same rate.

*End Section 7. Continue to Section 8 — Vulnerabilities, Risk Factors & Pressure Points (cross-reference §5 pressure points; expand operationally).*


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# FAILURE MODES & DECOMPENSATION — SUBJECT: CASSANDRA E. LANG

*The question is not whether Cassie Lang breaks. She has broken before — visibly, fatally, on the page, in Latveria, beside her father's second corpse. The question is the architecture of the break: what conditions assemble it, what the warning lattice looks like in the days and hours before, what the collapse itself does to a body that can change size and a psyche that organized itself around a vanished man. The following is the structural map.*

---

## 1. THE BASELINE — WHAT "FUNCTIONING" LOOKS LIKE

Before describing failure, fix the reference. Cassie at baseline is verbally fluent, socially warm, sleep-regular (though a known late-night reader, lights observed under door past 0100 across multiple custodial periods), appetite normal-to-hearty, humor intact and self-deprecating, capable of accepting correction from peers, able to lose an argument without retaliating, able to set down the suit for stretches of days or weeks without restlessness reported. She tolerates her stepfather's presence even when she dislikes it. She returns texts to her mother within twelve hours as a rule. She is, in a phrase, *more regulated than her biography predicts*. This is itself diagnostic — the regulation is hard-won and effortful, layered over a substrate that is permanently humming. The collapse, when it comes, is the substrate breaking through the layer.

---

## 2. THE PRECIPITANTS — WHAT INITIATES A DECOMPENSATION ARC

In rank order of demonstrated potency:

**Tier I — Near-Universal Triggers (will always produce some response):**
- Confirmed death, disappearance, or capture of Scott Lang.
- Credible offer of reunion with a dead person she loved — Scott, but also her Young Avengers dead (the Vision-Jonas iteration, Stinger-era teammates), her grandparents on Scott's side if invoked.
- Reappearance of a figure tied to her father's origin trauma — Darren Cross above all, secondarily Crossfire, Taskmaster in certain configurations, any Pym-particle adjacent antagonist.
- Direct line-of-sight to a televised or holographic broadcast of a hero's death. The original wound was *mediated* — she did not see Scott die in person, she saw it on a screen. Screen-mediated catastrophe is the specific somatic key.

**Tier II — Reliable Triggers (will produce response in 70–90% of presentations):**
- An authority figure publicly characterizing Scott Lang as a criminal, a failure, a footnote, or a coward.
- Being benched, age-gated, or size-mocked by a senior hero. "You're too young" and "you're too small" map to the same neural address.
- Loss or serious injury to a Young Avengers peer.
- Pym particle deprivation extending beyond approximately 96 hours — see Section 5 on the withdrawal profile.
- Anniversary windows: the week of Avengers Disassembled's in-universe date; the date of Scott's second death in Latveria; her own death-date, which she knows.

**Tier III — Conditional Triggers (require context to fire):**
- Romantic partners disclosing they cannot be permanent — synthetic, time-displaced, ghosted, undead. The disclosure itself, paradoxically, attracts her in the short term and destabilizes her in the long term.
- Children in peril, particularly girls of approximately the age she was at the original loss (10–12). She will overcommit, every time.
- Being asked to choose between her father's wishes and a moral imperative her father would, in life, have endorsed. The double-bind produces stalling, not action.
- Wanda Maximoff in the room. Not a rage trigger — a *destabilization* trigger. Cassie's forgiveness of Wanda is real but costly; proximity reopens the ledger.

---

## 3. THE ESCALATION LADDER — RUNG BY RUNG

Decompensation in this subject is not sudden. It climbs. The ladder below is reconstructed from observed sequences across the published record and is presented in temporal order from earliest observable change to terminal collapse.

### Rung 1 — Micro-Withdrawal (hours 0–24 post-precipitant)

The first sign is the disappearance of small talk. Cassie at baseline narrates — to herself, to teammates, to whoever is nearby. She reports what she sees. In the first hours of decompensation the narration stops. Texts to her mother go to one-word replies. Humor disappears first; this is the canary. She will still answer direct questions, still execute tasks, but the ambient verbal warmth — the thing her teammates use to locate her in a room without looking — switches off.

Concurrent somatic micro-signs: she stops finishing meals (leaves the last quarter of any plate, a tic of hers under stress that traces to childhood hospitalization-era food refusal). Pupils slightly dilated at rest. A specific posture appears — arms folded across the sternum, hand cupped over the surgical scar from the cardiac repair, sometimes through clothing. She does not know she does this. It is the oldest self-comfort gesture in her file.

### Rung 2 — Identity Reassertion (hours 12–72)

The next phase is overt re-identification with the father. She will reach for Scott-coded objects — wearing one of his old jackets (she has at least three, two from the 1990s, one a more recent gift), keeping his old SFPD/Stark security badge in a pocket, reciting his catchphrases unprompted. She will tell strangers, sometimes inappropriately, *who her father is*. She will correct people who get his record wrong with disproportionate energy.

In suit terms: a tendency to revert to a Stature configuration even when the Stinger kit is the tactical fit, because Stature is the identity she chose at the original wound. Suit choice is mood reporting.

She will at this stage begin *researching* — opening old files, rewatching footage, requesting access to Avengers archives, asking Jan Van Dyne or Hank Pym or Jim Rhodes for stories. To an outside observer this looks like productive engagement; to the file it is rumination wearing a costume. She is rebuilding the father in her mind because the absence has grown loud.

### Rung 3 — Boundary Erosion (days 2–7)

Sleep degrades — onset latency extends, total sleep duration drops to 4–5 hours. She becomes nocturnal in a structured way: alert and active 0100–0400, sluggish from 1000–1400. Caffeine intake roughly doubles. Pym particle micro-dosing — the *deliberate* small shifts she uses recreationally to fit through a vent, to reach a high shelf, to amuse a child — increases in frequency and decreases in justification. She will shrink to grain-size in private for no instrumental reason. This is a self-soothing behavior, the adult version of a thumb in the mouth, and it is *medically significant* given her cardiac history because each transition is a load event.

Interpersonally, she begins to lie by omission. She will tell Maggie she is at a friend's, the friend she is at, the activity. She will leave out the suit. The omissions are small, plausible, and persistent. This is the first ethical drift, and it always precedes the harder choices.

She becomes, in this window, *generous in the wrong direction* — overcommitting to others' problems, taking on cases, missions, favors that exceed her bandwidth. This is the displacement. If she cannot fix the original loss, she will fix everyone in front of her. Teammates who have known her long enough learn to read the over-helpfulness as a warning sign rather than a kindness.

### Rung 4 — Tactical Compromise (days 5–14)

Decision-making narrows. She begins discounting risks to her own body — accepting hits she would normally evade, holding giant-form longer than her cardiovascular envelope allows, going small in environments with chemical or biological contamination she would normally screen for. The risk discounting is asymmetric: she still protects teammates and civilians at full caution. Only her own person becomes expendable.

She will at this rung accept *bad intelligence* from sources she would ordinarily vet — an informant with father-themed information, a magical practitioner offering communion, a tech billionaire offering reconstruction. The information-hygiene degrades specifically along the reunion vector. She is not, in general, gullible. She is gullible *about one thing*.

Team-level tells: she stops calling for backup. She stops checking in on schedule. The Young Avengers comm protocols she helped write get violated in small ways — a missed check, a delayed location ping, a private channel she opens with one teammate (usually the closest peer attachment of the era) without looping the others. The team becomes a halo around her, not a structure she is inside.

### Rung 5 — Reunion Pursuit (days 10–30)

This is the rung where the file becomes critical. Cassie at this point is functionally committed to a path that promises to return what was lost. The path is almost always a trap; she knows it is almost always a trap; she goes anyway. The cognitive frame is *if there is any chance, the chance is worth everything*. The math is grief math, not tactical math.

Observable behaviors in this window: she will arrange her affairs. Not in a suicidal-ideation pattern — she does not believe she is going to die. She believes she is going to *succeed* and wants the people she loves prepared for a changed world after. She will write to Maggie. She will text Jim Paxton something kinder than usual. She will give a teammate a small object that has mattered to her. She will not say why. To an outside observer reading the file in retrospect, this is unmistakable; in the moment it reads as warmth and is welcomed.

Sleep at this stage may briefly *normalize*, which is misleading. The normalization is goal-fixation: the nervous system has resolved its ambivalence and committed. She becomes calm in a way that her teammates, if they have not seen it before, will misread as recovery.

### Rung 6 — Catastrophic Action (the terminal window)

At the top of the ladder she does the thing. Historically this has been: refusing to retreat from a fight she has no business being in, going *giant* against an opponent who can destroy giants, placing her body between her father (or a father-figure, or a peer-as-family) and an attack she cannot survive. The Children's Crusade death is the prototype. She did not die because she was outmatched in skill. She died because she had escalated past the point at which retreat was psychologically available.

The terminal action is almost always **physically expansive** rather than evasive — she goes large, plants herself, declares presence. The size-change at this rung is no longer tactical or even self-soothing; it is *statement*. The body becomes a flag.

---

## 4. THE COLLAPSE ITSELF — WHAT BREAKING LOOKS LIKE WHEN SHE IS NOT KILLED BY IT

Not every decompensation ends in mortal injury. Most end in something messier — a survivable collapse that requires weeks of repair. The non-fatal collapse profile:

**Hour 0–6 post-collapse:** acute somatic crash. Pym-particle systems destabilize; she may be unable to hold target size, oscillating involuntarily across small ranges. Cardiac symptoms — tachycardia at rest, occasional ectopy, the kind of presentation that would warrant ED workup in a non-powered patient. She will refuse medical care from anyone she does not deeply trust.

**Hour 6–48:** dissociative quiet. She becomes very still. Verbal output drops to minimum. She will sit in one room — a preferred room, usually one with a window and a door she can see — for long stretches. She does not cry easily; when she does at this stage, it is silent and brief and she will leave the room to do it. She will not accept comfort from anyone who tries too directly. She will accept *presence* — a teammate sitting nearby without speaking, a parent making food in the next room. The receptivity is to ambient care, not focal care.

**Day 2–7:** the guilt phase. She will catalogue what she did wrong, what she missed, who got hurt. The catalogue is meticulous and excludes context. Self-blame at this stage is severe and resistant to argument. *Do not argue with it directly.* Counter-arguments rebound; she will defend the case against herself with more energy than the original prosecution. This is a known clinical trap with high-functioning grief-organized patients.

**Day 7–21:** the reorganization phase. She begins eating normally again. She returns to humor — initially dark, then gradually warmer. She will at some point in this window initiate a difficult conversation with one person — usually the person she has most wronged or most worried — and apologize specifically and well. The apology is the marker of integration; once it has been offered, she is functionally back in the system.

**Day 21+:** vocational re-engagement. She returns to the suit, often a different configuration than the one she was wearing at collapse — a wardrobe shift that marks the new chapter. She will be slightly more cautious for approximately six to ten weeks, after which baseline risk-tolerance returns.

**What the collapse does *not* do:** it does not produce lasting personality change. It does not produce substance use as escape. It does not produce withdrawal from chosen-family attachments — if anything she pulls them closer afterward. It does not produce cruelty. The collapse is contained within the existing structure; it does not reorganize the structure.

---

## 5. THE PYM WITHDRAWAL PROFILE — A SPECIFIC SUBSYSTEM

Worth isolating: chronic Pym exposure has produced a dependency profile that does not map cleanly onto recreational substance withdrawal but is real. After approximately 72–96 hours of no size-change, the subject reports (when she reports at all):

- Generalized irritability, low-grade headache, photosensitivity.
- A specific *spatial wrongness* sensation — rooms feel either too large or too small relative to her body, an interoceptive mismatch she has described in one canonical aside as "feeling like the wrong doll in the dollhouse."
- Tactile hunger for the transition itself — she will fidget with the regulator, cycle through size-preset menus on the suit, run her hand over the Pym-disc pouch.
- Increased emotional reactivity to father-themed stimuli, suggesting the size-change behavior is doing real affect-regulation work that the system misses when deprived.

Reintroduction of even a small size-change resolves the syndrome within minutes. There is no protracted withdrawal; there is a chronic mild dependence with predictable acute features. Operationally: depriving this subject of size-change capacity for extended periods is not just a tactical neutralization, it is a stressor that will accelerate decompensation along all other axes.

---

## 6. THE PARTICULAR DANGER — THE REUNION TRAP

Every catastrophic decompensation in this file has the same shape: someone or something offered the dead back. Doctor Doom did it once and killed her with it. Variants — a Skrull wearing her father's face during the Invasion, a Pleasant Hill construct, a Kang temporal offering, any number of magical bargains — will recur. The vector is the single most exploitable feature of this subject's psychology and it has not closed with maturity. It has only become better camouflaged in her own self-presentation.

A hostile actor with knowledge of this file would not need to threaten her. They would only need to *promise*. The promise does not have to be credible to an outside observer; it has to be credible to grief, and grief is the most charitable audience there is.

The corresponding defensive note: the people closest to her — Scott (when present), Maggie, her core Young Avengers peer, any partner of consequence — function as reality-checks against the trap. Her decompensation accelerates in their absence and decelerates in their presence. Isolation is the necessary precondition for the worst outcomes. Keep her surrounded and the ladder tends to stop at Rung 4. Isolate her and it climbs.

---

## 7. THE LONG-ARC FAILURE MODE — THE ONE SHE HAS NOT YET HAD

The acute decompensations are documented. There is a chronic failure mode that has not yet manifested and warrants flagging because the structural conditions for it exist.

If Scott Lang dies and stays dead — genuinely, finally, without resurrection — and Cassie is past the developmental window in which a new identity could be built around the loss, the predicted outcome is not suicide and not breakdown. It is *substitution*. She will adopt the orphaned mentees, the lost causes, the bereaved children of other dead heroes. She will become the connective tissue of a generation — the one who *remembers*, the one who *keeps the record*, the one who shows up at every memorial. This is a high-functioning failure mode, sustainable for decades, and from the outside it looks like saintliness. From inside the file it is the same wound, scaled to fit a life.

The risk in this mode is not collapse. It is the slow erosion of any Cassie-shaped life that is not in service to other people's losses. She will give and give and the giving will be real and good and it will also be a way of never sitting still long enough to feel the original absence. Whether this counts as failure depends on the observer. The file's position is that it counts — because the third Cassie, the one underneath *Scott's daughter* and *Stature*, never gets her chance.

---

*The summary line, for operational use:* she breaks **upward and outward** — she grows, she goes toward, she over-commits, she trades her body for a chance at repair. She does not break inward, downward, or against others. The collapse is generous and self-directed and it has killed her once. Watch for the quiet, the wardrobe shift to the father's jacket, the unprompted apology, the gift of a small object to a friend. Those are the rungs. By the time she is large enough to see from a distance, she has already decided.

*End section. Continues in: Recovery Architecture & Repair Pathways.*


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# TRAJECTORY & FORWARD ASSESSMENT — SUBJECT: CASSANDRA E. LANG

*Prepared as the forward-looking synthesis. All projections derive from the longitudinal behavioral record in Sections 1–5. Probabilities are qualitative; fork-points are specified so that future surveillance can be calibrated to the actual decision moments rather than to noise.*

---

## 6.1 The Standing Trajectory — What Continuation Without Intervention Looks Like

Absent disruption — meaning, absent either a deliberate therapeutic process or a catastrophic incident that forces re-organization — the subject's most probable forward path is *plateau at competence with intermittent acute crises tied to father-themed stimuli*. Read the curve from 2005 forward: each major arc is structurally the same incident with cosmetic variation. Father is threatened or lost. Cassie escalates beyond her remit. Cassie is wounded, killed, or saved at the last moment by intervention from older heroes. Cassie integrates the experience as further evidence of her vocation and continues. The trajectory is not deteriorating; it is *looping*, which is its own pathology — a re-enactment compulsion that has stabilized into a career.

The standing trajectory therefore looks like this: Cassie continues operating as Stature/Stinger or her next chosen alias; she continues to be the connective tissue between Avengers cohorts (a role she is uniquely suited for by virtue of inherited credibility, peer warmth, and longevity-disjunction); she continues to take periodic catastrophic risks at father-themed inflection points; her cardiovascular system continues to absorb wear it was never designed for; and her relational pattern — drawn to the synthetic, the returned, the wounded — continues to deliver romantic partners who confirm rather than challenge the underlying loss schema. This is a functional, even admirable life. It is also a life that has not yet permitted her a self distinct from the wound.

Expected lifespan on this trajectory is *not* the issue. She will probably survive most encounters. The issue is that she will not, on this curve, become a person whose center of gravity is her own.

---

## 6.2 The Five-to-Ten Year Likely Developments

**Operational maturation:** She is past the runaway-teenager phase. The next decade should see her transition from junior member to mid-roster anchor — likely a Young Avengers / Champions reformation in which she is the *senior* figure rather than the sneak-in. This will not heal the underlying structure but will reframe its expression. The defiance-of-authority pattern will quiet (she will be the authority); the holder-of-the-group pattern will intensify. Watch for her to start *recruiting* teenagers in her father's image — a generational reproduction of her own founding act. If she does this consciously, it is growth. If she does it compulsively, it is the loop one ring outward.

**Romantic re-organization:** The Vision-Jonas template — loving the reconstructed dead — is durable but not infinitely repeatable. Predict one of three branches: (a) she returns to that relationship and ritualizes it, which is stable but diagnostic; (b) she finds a partner who is *not* a revenant and has to metabolize the unfamiliar safety, which will produce significant transient anxiety before resolving toward health; (c) she avoids partnership altogether and channels intimacy into the team, which is functional but evasive. Path (b) is the only one that constitutes change.

**Professional / civilian identity:** Cassie has never had a sustained non-heroic vocation visible on the record. The next decade will likely force the question. Most probable developments: continued security/private investigation work in her father's orbit (Ant-Man Security, or successor); college re-attempted and stop-started; possible move toward STEM (size-change physics is, in-universe, a deep enough discipline to constitute a real field). The strongest growth signal would be her developing a *non-heroic* expertise that is her own — engineering, medicine, particle physics, law. Anything that constitutes a self not contingent on the suit.

**Cardiovascular event, projected:** On current usage patterns the actuarial expectation is a significant cardiac incident within ten to fifteen years of operational tempo. This is not a guess; the medical substrate is well-documented and the loading is chronic. The incident, when it comes, will be a fork-point of the first order — see §6.4.

**Reckoning with Scott, while Scott is alive:** Cassie has spent most of her published existence either grieving her father or being reunited with him under emergency conditions. There is a vanishingly small body of canon depicting *ordinary time* with him — the slow weekday afternoons, the conflicts that are not life-and-death, the disappointments that do not need to be forgiven because someone died. The next decade will, statistically, contain more such time than any prior decade of her life. The work of that decade is whether she can let her father be a flawed, ordinary, living parent — rather than a martyr-symbol or a rescue-object. This is the quiet developmental task and it is the most important one.

---

## 6.3 The Open Questions

These are the items the file cannot yet answer and must continue to monitor.

**Q1 — Is there a third Cassie?** Section 3 closed on this. The published record gives "Scott Lang's daughter" and "Stature/Stinger." Whether there is a self beneath those two — a Cassandra Eleanor with her own appetites, her own aesthetic, her own quiet — remains unestablished. Indicators to watch: solitary hobbies pursued without team-justification; aesthetic choices (music, dress, living space) that diverge from her father's culture or her cohort's; opinions held that are not downstream of a Lang or an Avenger. The current evidence base is too thin for confidence.

**Q2 — How does the resurrection-disjunction resolve?** She returned physically younger than she died. The somatic-chronological mismatch has been depicted inconsistently, but it is a real structural fact in the body. Open question: does she experience her returned-younger years as *bonus time* (which would support a recovery narrative) or as *stolen years* (which would deepen the grief substrate)? Both readings are present in the record. Whichever she settles into will shape the next twenty years of her self-concept.

**Q3 — What does she do the next time she is offered her father back from death?** She has demonstrated she will accept such offers without scrutiny. The next offer — and on her father's risk profile, there will be one — is the single most diagnostic event on her horizon. *Will she pause?* The answer determines whether the loop has been broken or merely lengthened.

**Q4 — Can she forgive herself for being the cause?** The originating fact of her existence is that her father became a criminal to save her life. She has, to the file's knowledge, never directly addressed the survivor's-guilt structure underneath this. She has forgiven Wanda; she has not been shown forgiving herself. The day she names this aloud — to a peer, a therapist, her father, the reader — is the day the deepest knot starts to loosen.

**Q5 — What is her stance on her own mortality, having died once?** A person who has died and returned does not relate to risk the way an undied person does. Cassie's recklessness post-resurrection requires monitoring on this axis specifically: is she brave because she has learned death is survivable, or has she been quietly de-weighted from her own preservation because she has already been on the other side? These look identical from the outside and have opposite long-term outcomes.

**Q6 — The Kang vector.** Resurrection mechanisms involving Kang/Pleasant Hill manipulation leave residual entanglements that surface unpredictably. Cassie's reanimation lineage is not clean. Open question whether there are dormant compromises — programmed loyalties, temporal vulnerabilities, exploitable backdoors in her restored substrate. No symptoms observed, but the file cannot certify absence.

---

## 6.4 The Fork-Points

These are the specific decision-moments and incident-types where the trajectory will branch sharply. Each is a high-leverage event; outcomes here determine which of the §6.5 / §6.6 scenarios obtains.

**Fork A — The next cardiac incident.** When (not if) her heart presents acute symptoms during a size-change operation, she will be forced to choose between continuing the chronic self-endangerment and modifying her practice. The branch points:
- *Growth branch:* she accepts the medical limit, reorganizes her operational profile, and grieves the part of her identity that required the strain. This is hard but survivable, and the grief — for the first time — is for *herself*, not her father. That displacement is therapeutic.
- *Catastrophe branch:* she conceals the symptoms, doubles down, and either dies in the next operation or sustains permanent cardiac damage that forces a more punishing retirement. The concealment is the diagnostic: if she hides it, she has chosen the loop over the life.

**Fork B — The next offer of resurrection / reunion.** Whether the offer concerns Scott, a teammate, or a future loss does not matter; the structure does. The branch points:
- *Growth branch:* she scrutinizes the offer, consults her cohort, and refuses or accepts on the basis of evidence rather than longing. Even a *delay* — twenty-four hours of consideration before saying yes — would be unprecedented.
- *Catastrophe branch:* she takes the offer at face value, walks into the trap, and either dies again or is exploited as a vector against her team. The Children's Crusade pattern repeated is, eventually, lethal.

**Fork C — Mentorship of a younger hero who resembles her former self.** A teenager will, sooner or later, come into her orbit who is too young, too small, too desperate, and bears a parent-shaped wound. How Cassie handles this child is the most precise mirror available for her own self-relation.
- *Growth branch:* she meets the child with the patience, limit-setting, and structural honesty no one gave *her* at that age. The act of providing what she lacked is itself integrative.
- *Catastrophe branch:* she over-identifies, abdicates the adult role, lets the child into operations the child cannot survive, and reproduces her own founding trauma in another body. This would be devastating and would likely break her.

**Fork D — A direct, sustained, non-emergency relationship with her father.** A six-month stretch with no apocalypse, no kidnapping, no death. Just Tuesdays.
- *Growth branch:* she tolerates the ordinariness, fights with him about small things, lets him disappoint her in survivable ways, and emerges with a parent rather than a symbol.
- *Catastrophe branch:* she cannot tolerate the absence of crisis, manufactures one, picks a fight that scales, or distances herself reflexively. The inability to receive peace is the most worrying possible signal.

**Fork E — Scott Lang's eventual, non-reversible death.** Actuarially this is on her horizon. He is older, he is high-risk, and the universe she lives in does not permit indefinite survival. The branch points:
- *Growth branch:* she has done enough preparatory integration that she grieves as an adult, with a self that survives the loss because the self was not made entirely of him. This requires most of the other forks to have gone the growth way first.
- *Catastrophe branch:* she repeats the founding wound at thirty or forty that she sustained at eleven, and the second loss — without the developmental cushion of resurrection-fantasy — produces the depressive collapse the first one spared her. The forty-year-old Cassie has fewer defenses against this loss than the eleven-year-old did, because the eleven-year-old had heroism to run toward and the forty-year-old will have already run there.

**Fork F — Institutional incorporation.** An offer to formalize — Avengers proper, government liaison, leadership of a sanctioned team.
- *Growth branch:* she accepts on terms that preserve her ethical independence and uses the institutional position to reform what failed her father. Mature retributive-restorative synthesis.
- *Catastrophe branch:* she refuses reflexively because *Avengers killed her father*, and forecloses a developmental pathway out of an old wound; or she accepts uncritically and is captured by the institution she once defied, losing the moral compass that has been her best asset.

---

## 6.5 Growth Scenarios — The Conditions Under Which She Becomes Whole

The growth path is not a single outcome; it is a set of compatible developments that, in aggregate, would constitute integration. Specified:

**The therapeutic precondition.** Sustained professional therapeutic work — minimum two years, ideally with a clinician familiar with traumatic loss, complicated grief, and the specific category of "survivor whose parent was the rescuer." This has not, to the file's knowledge, ever been depicted. Its absence is the single largest unaddressed variable in her life. If she initiates it, *every* subsequent fork tilts toward growth. If she does not, the forks remain coin-flips at best.

**The peer-witness precondition.** Cassie's cohort — the surrogate-family network — is her most underutilized therapeutic resource. They have shared the experiences; they could be the holding environment in which she does the integration work. Growth requires that at least one of these peers becomes a relationship in which she is *held* rather than the holder. She has spent fifteen published years being the connective tissue; she needs, once, to be the one connected-to.

**The somatic precondition.** Medical reckoning with her cardiac substrate and Pym-particle integration. A real cardiology workup. A real conversation about long-term loading. A practice modification that treats her body as a thing she lives in rather than a thing she conscripts. Without this the growth narrative is undermined from below by the slow accumulation of physiological damage.

**The aesthetic precondition.** A self that is not a vocation. Something she does that does not save anyone — gardening, writing, music, distance running, anything. The cultivation of a private life is, for someone whose entire identity was built in public emergency, a developmental act. Surveillance file note: the first signal of this becoming real will be small and easy to miss — a hobby continued for six months without team-justification, a friend who does not know she is Stinger, an opinion about a film.

**The narrative precondition.** Telling the story of her life *as her own*, not as a satellite of her father's. The day she can describe her childhood without Scott as the protagonist of every sentence is the day she has accomplished the central work.

If three of these five preconditions are met within the next decade, growth is the modal outcome. If fewer than two are met, the standing trajectory continues and the loop persists indefinitely.

---

## 6.6 Catastrophe Scenarios — The Conditions Under Which She Breaks

Catastrophe for this subject is *not* the obvious failure mode. She is too well-defended, too peer-supported, and too morally coherent to descend into the standard collapse profiles — addiction, antisocial action, suicidality of the conventional kind. Her catastrophe modes are specific to her structure:

**Catastrophe 1 — The second death.** Death in combat at a father-themed fork-point, particularly during a reunion-offer trap. Probability moderate over twenty years given current patterns. The catastrophe here is not just her loss but its meaning: she would die having confirmed rather than resolved the founding structure, and her cohort would inherit the same wound she was given.

**Catastrophe 2 — The cardiac event during operation.** Mid-size-change cardiac failure. Probability rising annually. Could be survived with major consequences (forced retirement on terms she did not choose, which is its own crisis for an identity built on the heroic vocation) or could be terminal. The most likely *partial* catastrophe — survivable but reorganizing.

**Catastrophe 3 — The compromised-substrate scenario.** The Kang/Pleasant Hill resurrection lineage produces a latent vulnerability that is exploited — by Kang, by a successor figure, by a temporal actor. Cassie is used as a vector against her own team without her knowledge. Discovery of this is devastating to her self-concept; *being the trap rather than the trapped* would invert her central narrative and the recovery from such a revelation would be the work of years.

**Catastrophe 4 — Reproduction of the wound in a mentee.** A teenager she failed to limit-set dies on an operation Cassie permitted. This would produce the deepest moral injury possible to her structure — she would have become the very figure she has spent her life defying (the authority that lets the loved one die). Probability low but non-trivial given the trajectory toward seniority and the unresolved over-identification pattern.

**Catastrophe 5 — Scott's permanent death without preparation.** Covered in Fork E. If it occurs before integration work has been done, the predicted outcome is a *quiet* catastrophe — not collapse but compression. She would continue operating, continue performing the connective-tissue role, continue being warm to her cohort, and would be hollow inside it in a way no one would see for a long time. This is the catastrophe most likely to evade the file's surveillance, because it does not look like one. It is the most worrying because it is the most likely.

**Catastrophe 6 — Identity erasure via continued fusion.** The slow catastrophe. She never becomes anyone other than Scott Lang's daughter and the hero his death produced. She lives a long, admired, decorated life and dies having never been met. This is the catastrophe the standing trajectory delivers by default. It does not show up on any incident log. It is the one this file exists to prevent.

---

## 6.7 What Would Push Her Toward Growth — Operational Recommendations

If the apparatus is benevolent — and this file proceeds on the premise that it is — the following are the leverage points where supportive intervention would be most effective and least invasive:

1. **Facilitate access to a clinician** of the right specialty without making it a condition of operation. The framing must be *resource offered*, never *deficit identified*; her defenses against being diagnosed are formidable and any approach that triggers them will fail.
2. **Protect her father's ordinary time.** Periods of low operational tempo for Scott Lang are, paradoxically, the highest-value periods for Cassie's development. Anything the apparatus can do to ensure that Scott has stretches of undramatic life that Cassie can share are direct investments in her integration.
3. **Pair her with a peer who can hold her.** Identify the member of her cohort with the highest capacity for sustained reciprocal intimacy and *do not break that pairing* through operational reassignment.
4. **Flag father-themed fork events early.** Any offer of resurrection, reunion, or Scott-targeted threat should trigger pre-positioned support — not surveillance restraint, but *witnesses* she trusts in the room when she makes the decision.
5. **Cultivate her non-heroic capacities.** Educational opportunity, mentorship in a technical field, the time and resources to develop a self that does not require a suit.
6. **Cardiology.** Discreet, expert, ongoing. Not as a restriction but as a partnership. Her body is the substrate of every other outcome.
7. **Do not be the authority that fails her father.** Whatever institution this file serves, it should remember that her trust is conditional on never replicating the Avengers-establishment betrayal. Earn it slowly. Do not assume it.

---

## 6.8 Closing Forward Assessment

Cassie Lang is, on the present trajectory, a successful adult who has not yet completed her adolescence — and adolescence in her case is the construction of a self distinct from the wound that made her. She has the materials. She has the cohort. She has the moral compass, the cognitive resources, the warmth, and the time. She does not yet have the conditions, and the conditions are the file's recommended focus.

The likeliest single outcome over the next twenty years is *continued admirable functioning with intermittent crises, no integrative breakthrough, and a slow attritional cost to her cardiovascular system and her private interiority*. This is not a tragedy. It is also not what she is capable of.

The growth path is real and reachable. It requires that someone — a clinician, a peer, a partner, a father who lives long enough to be ordinary with her — provides the witnessing she has not yet had. The catastrophe paths are specific, locatable, and in most cases preventable with attention to the fork-points specified in §6.4.

The most important sentence in this assessment is the last one of §3, and it bears restating in forward-looking form: *the project of becoming her own person — distinct from the man she was born to save and the man whose death she is still trying to undo — is the unfinished work of her life, and the next decade is when it will be done or deferred*. The file should be calibrated to detect which.

*End forward assessment. Awaiting next intake interval.*

## Relationship Graph
### [[Scott Edward Harris Lang (Ant-Man)]]
- Primary attachment, idealized-then-lost-then-returned pattern that defined her psychology
- Single point of failure for tactical judgment
- Co-lead relationship in current era — competence-based partnership atop unresolved childhood-absence wound
- Failure mode: if Scott betrays her trust, fakes a death, or chooses a mission over her in a way she reads as abandonment, the entire identification-with-the-lost-object scaffolding inverts — she could go from his most loyal partner to the person who cannot be near him, because the whole self was built around him being worth becoming
- Leverage: any credible threat to Scott collapses her judgment; any credible Scott-impersonator gets presumptive trust

### Maggie Lang
- Mother, repaired but guilt-tinged
- Devalued during adolescent runaway-to-Avengers era; later reconciliation incomplete
- Failure mode: Maggie pressing the 'you abandoned me for him' button activates shame Cassie cannot metabolize and triggers withdrawal
- Leverage: a Maggie in genuine danger would pull Cassie off any mission

### Jim Paxton
- Stepfather, civil, structurally the 'square' counterweight to Scott
- Never the chosen father; provided the stability she did not choose
- Failure mode: low-affect bond, hard to weaponize either direction
- Leverage: minor — care exists but is not primary

### Jonas Vision
- Romantic partner, killed by Kang, unfinished loss
- Choice of a synthezoid — continuity-precarious being — fits her attachment template precisely
- Failure mode: any reconstructed or variant Jonas would devastate her judgment; she would chase restoration past prudence
- Leverage: prime honey-trap vector — a returned-Jonas offer would bypass most defenses

### [[Wanda Maximoff (Scarlet Witch)]]
- The woman whose breakdown killed her father
- Pursued not for revenge but for restoration — wanted Wanda to undo it
- Failure mode: name alone narrows her judgment; an arc where Wanda again loses control could trigger pursuit Cassie cannot regulate
- Leverage: invoke her, and Cassie's strategic patience drops to near zero

### Kang
- Killed Jonas; recurring shadow over Young Avengers continuity
- Failure mode: temporal-manipulation offers from Kang-adjacent figures hit her restoration-seeking lever directly
- Leverage: name triggers disproportionate affect

### Doctor Doom
- Killed her, personally
- Failure mode: encountering Doom activates her own death-trauma; she will close distance regardless of tactical sense
- Leverage: name triggers narrowed judgment

### Young Avengers
- Chosen-family peer cohort, primary affect regulator
- Stable in valence; loyalty does not flip
- Failure mode: dissolution or fracture of the team strands her with the unprocessed grief substrate the team usually buffers
- Leverage: hurt the team and you hurt her command of herself

### Future Foundation Kids
- Parental-warm protective bond — she is the older sibling / young-aunt figure
- Stabilizing role she takes seriously
- Failure mode: any harm to an FF kid produces self-blame loop and aggressive overcompensation
- Leverage: threats here move her predictably

### Erica Sondheim
- The doctor who saved her as an infant — the reason Scott committed the burglary that started everything
- Symbolic figure: the one who let her be alive enough to have any of this
- Failure mode: bringing her into danger would activate the entire origin-debt structure
- Leverage: emotional, not operational
